RATING: 4
Flsah Point: Fire Rescue could be used as a synonym for a boring game. Everyone is given a special ability which pretty much nails down what you do in the game. This results in zero decision making during the game, which equals getting bored. Moreover, the ratio between play time and administrative tasks (i.e. rolling dice to determine locations for new outbursts of smoke and flame and points of interest) is way off. Your turn is over in 5 seconds while all the dice rolling between turns takes 20-30 seconds per turn.

Otherwise the game works just fine and there are no apparent flaws in it. It just is not fun, since there is hardly anything to do. Probably the best quality of the game is that the promised 45min playing time seems to be quite close to reality.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
A theme that shines brightly, clean layout and typography that just "flows" and makes sense, well-crafted components, awesome fire mechanic.... what's not to love?! My wife and I instantly fell in love with this on our first play, and I can't wait to get it to the table again. It plays quickly, the rules make sense, and it feels very intimate.

FP:FR gets compared to Pandemic a lot, and rightly so. It shares several aspects and mechanics that work very well. However, while I adore Pandemic and it's expansions, FP:FR has a lot to recommend it as well. This shouldn't be an either/or decision, but rather, get both! Pandemic feels massive, a global fight for survival. FP:FR feels very personal, a rapidly-changing struggle to save victims in a burning house. The difference in scale/scope is notable, and both do their jobs well.

Get Flash Point. If you enjoy co-op gaming at ALL, FP:FR will scratch the itch.

RATING: 5
A promising game that suffers from rules clarification bonanza. A problem that occurs frequently when written by designers that don't bother about prove-reading and others to test play after reading rules by themselves. 

A cooperative game that test your logic against the game system. The game system for fire spread depends on adjacency. So concentrating specific square to clear fire can limit damage and spread. Spending a few turns to clear fire instead of helping victims seem to be a good strategy in game terms. 

Very luck dependent as the dice does all the talking. But strange if fire begins again from a room that is cleared with 'water and engine hose'. Very gamey, similarity to real life situation is moderate at best. Thus the game make you feel that the fire fighters are the only one doing the job while the others sit and watch outside....even if the building collapses. 

Interesting first game....Same downward spiral in the next following game.....did not want to play a third. Average game that will rate badly as you play more.

RATING: 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
This game gets compared to Pandemic a lot, so I'll start with that.  It's a cooperative game, where each player's turn consists of taking a few basic actions, followed by a progression of bad stuff where you randomly select a location and increment the bad stuff there, or, if the bad stuff is already maximized there, spread the bad stuff to the surrounding locations. The team consists of specialists, most of which have an advantage when doing one of the basic things, and your actions help you towards "winning the game" or "not losing the game, giving you more time to win the game". Usually, even when you think you're winning, a few "progression of bad stuff" turns in a row will go horribly wrong, and you'll lose the game every damn time, in an always tense and sometimes frustrating way, the latter case being followed by swearing and muttering about bad luck.

So yes, it's just a little bit like Pandemic.  If you're looking to buy Flash Point, how you feel about Pandemic is probably a damn good indicator of how you'll feel about Flash Point (I think I slightly prefer Flash Point, but it's close).  The main points of difference:

1) More players.  Pandemic is designed for 2-4, and you can do 5 if you really want.  Flash Point says 1-6 on the box (although 1 or 2 sounds downright miserable without multiple characters per player), and you could probably go all the way to 8 (the number of different characters available).  As I frequently game with 5-6, this is a positive for me.

2) More setup.  I was always a bit annoyed by the need to separate out the deck and shuffle 4-6 smaller decks in Pandemic.  However, Flash Point, not having cards, requires that you first start off by randomly rolling for initial fire placement (3 explosions start the game, each of which has slightly different rules for placement) and the appropriate damage and fire tokens, followed by hazmat placement, hot spot placement, and initial victim placement.  On the medium difficulty setting, you'll throw the dice 16 times before you even start the game.

3) More differences between characters.  Because Flash Point allows you to switch between characters mid-game, it's more appropriate for the characters to have more specialized abilities than in Pandemic.  The specialization, combined with the ability to store actions also creates new opportunities for coordination (e.g., the Paramedic delays her turn so the CAFS guy can clear a path to the victim for her).  However, some characters are so specialized that nobody else should bother doing their action, and/or they should do nothing but that action (I'm looking at you, Driver), which somewhat limits the reasonable tactical decisions.

4) A clear path to victory.  In Pandemic, since I don't know who is going to draw what color cards, and it's a pain in the ass to pass cards anyways, I frequently can't make any progress towards winning the game on my turn.  In Flash Point, there are 3 victims in play.  To help win the game, get to them or help somebody else get to them.  It's that straightforward.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Awesome!  This game just drips theme, and that theme is well supported by the mechanisms of play.  

Each turn you really feel as though, you are battling overwhelming odds, in a desperate battle to rescue the victims from a house fire.  The mechanisms to advance the fire, including explosions, hazardous materials, damaged walls and doors, smoke and ever-expanding fire, gives it such a feeling of tension.  All the time you are balancing decisions about how best to use your actions; do I extinguish that fire or do I try to rescue the victim and let the fire rage?

It plays 1-6 players in around 30-40 mins, is simple to learn, with many ways to increase difficulty.

I'm a huge fan of Pandemic but this game has now surpassed it.  Whist it is not as tight and clever, the fire-fighting theme is an instant grabber for non-gamers, providing quick entry and easy understanding. 

I'm delighted I joined the Kickstarter program with this one, the artwork and production is beautiful and it came with fire-meeples and the Urban Structures expansion.

If you like family games that aren't competitive, then this is a near perfect gateway game to the world of co-operative play.  

If you are already a fan of co-ops, this game is a MUST buy.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

In any case it is a great game, and I saved myself from getting sick of it.

RATING: 6.5
Kickstarted.

I played it once and was just underwhelmed. We had an alright time with it, but it was more about the jokes we got to make along the way (like when my friend tried to rescue someone, wound up right beside them, and then watched as they got engulfed in flame before their eyes [tragic, I know, but cardboard people are cardboard people], or what a big deal I made out of making sure we had to save the cat). The game itself didn't hold me at all. Fire is entirely random, which is neat, but at the same time it's not necessarily exciting. I also found that I really disliked that, not only do you have the option to switch roles during the course of the game, but it's practically a necessary thing to do. I felt so disconnected from the pieces I was moving around when I went from being a paramedic to a deck gunner to something else. I guess I wanted to feel like I was one of the characters, and I wanted to play my role, but that was basically impossible (because you will need people who specialize at everything, and with too few players you won't get those roles. of course, if you have a full table of 6, so much happens between your turn and the next time you go that it's all but impossible to plan for most things).
Overall, it just wasn't for me. I can understand others liking it, and maybe some of the other maps would have been more interesting with their special rules, but the core of the game had no place in my heart.

Koop Spiel mit sehr gutem Solopotential.
Ich habe vor dem Kauf einige sehr positive Review gelesen und Videos angeschaut.
Das Spiel hatte als Kickstarterprojekt angefangen.
Das Spielmaterial in der deutschen Version sieht sehr gut aus. Anstelle der einfachen Holzmeepels gibt es hier farbige Feuerwehrmänner aus Weichplastik. Weiterhin haben die zu Rettenden alles Gesichter und nicht nur die Konturen der US-Version. 
Habe das Spiel Solo gespielt. Zum Einspielen in der einfachen Familienversion mit 2 Figuren (die trotzdem nur knapp gewonnen wurde weil mir das Haus fast über dem Kopf eingestürzt wäre). Und ein paarmal im ersten Expertenmodus mit 3 Figuren.
Thematisch ist dieses Spiel weit weniger abstrakt als Pandemie. Die Bedrohung durch das sich unvorhersehbar ausbreitende Feuer und möglichen Explosionen (bis hin zu verheerenden Kettenreaktionen) halten das Spannungsniveau recht hoch.
Auch mit einer Gruppe macht das Spiel Spaß (wenn denn die Mitspieler Koop mögen und ich mich nach dem anfänglichen Erklären der Regeln etwas beim Spielverlauf zurückhalte...).
Das Spielthema ist sicherlich herausragend aus der Menge der Koop-Spiele.
Hier gibt es eine ziemlich gut umgesetzte (kostenlose) Version zum Solospiel am PC als Java-Programm: [url=http://www.mediafire.com/?93km82o9tpd601p]Flash-Point Java[/url] 
Man sollte jedoch die Spielregeln schon etwas kennen bevor man das spielt.

und dabei auch die folgenden kleineren alten Erweiterung mit bestellt:
[thing=110139]Urban Structures[/thing]

RATING: 7
Good cooperative game with an approachable theme that is incorporated nicely into gameplay. Tension builds with the progression from smoke to fire to explosion with unpredictable chain reactions. The game allows players to be flexible by allowing them to switch special abilities mid-game and save action points for future turns.

Artwork is pretty bland. Because you can still win as long as you save a certain number of victims, it's sometimes in your best interest to give up on some victims if they are just not worth going after. Thematically, it's a little flawed because victims can be seen as expendable.

RATING: 7.5
Only a few plays in, so I can see the rating on this game going up.

Flash Point: Fire Rescue is a fun, fairly fast cooperative game that is mechanically very similar to Pandemic or Forbidden Island (which is a good thing, IMO).  The game looks great and gameplay moves along well.  The characters are also well done.  

I only have 2 real issues with this game:

1. The way Points of Interest are put on the board at random.  Whenever you take a POI (be it a person, pet, or false alarm) off the board, a new one is randomly put on, and this can be very immersion breaking.  You could have just gone through a small bathroom and now suddenly there is a person in there?  I get that this makes sense mechanically, given the size of the board, but it doesn't make much sense thematically.

2. This doesn't get to the table much.  When my group wants to play a coop game, we either go with Pandemic (which is a little heavier and longer) or Forbidden Island (which is a little lighter and shorter).  Flash Point falls in this middle ground where we say "well, if we are going to spend 45 minutes on a coop, it might as well be Pandemic".  

I definitely see this rating rising as I get it to the table more.

RATING: 8
April 2015:
My under 5 y.o. son and I watched a few games reviews to start a new bonding hobby together. We both got interested in the little fire fighters and it was our first pick at the FLGS. It clicked with us immediately and two new gamers were born on that day.

Flash Point is an excellent gateway game for the whole family. The theme is very engaging and it appeals to kids. I tweaked the rules to make it easier for my under 5 year old, but he is ready for family++ rules now (after less than 2 months). The difficulty scales up for adults and it plays solo nicely as well. Perhaps a bit random and swingy every so often (why would fire and victims pop up randomly here and there?), but I do not mind as it actually keeps adults as "helpless" as kids and lets them enjoy it together. Highly recommended!

June 2015:
Still enjoying it after many plays. However, I have been unlucky to set the difficulty too low on few occasions when playing with adults (or maybe dice just did not love us?) which made the game very mechanical, blunt and disengaging. Downgrading my rating from 9 to 8 as the sweet spot is a bit too fickly to find for my taste. But if you hit it, it can be a blast.

RATING: 9
Even at the Family Rules level, this is a really fun co-op, with lots of tension based on the die rolls, placement of POIs, and spreading mechanisms. I really like the simple Action Point system (reminiscent of Pandemic), especially that you can carry over a certain amount of AP to a future turn, not a lot of games allow that. Normally, my friends and I will play this at Expert for the variable character abilities, Hazmat rules, Healing, and so forth, but there's something in the box here for everyone, and where in lesser hands Flash Point might have trivialized the fire fighting profession, I feel this really does it a service without coming off as too cute or silly.

RATING: 7
Flash Point to me is kinda Pandemic meets ameritrash: in it, the elegant escalation mechanic of Pandemic is substituted by the randomness of dice rolls and, admittedly, by a much more appealing theme.

The family game, while not very deep from a gamer's perspective, is easy and smooth enough to be played with kids, and provides a fun challenge.

The expert game is much more challenging, and quite enjoyable even by gamers.

Rating is just a 6 for the family game, and 7 for the expert version. But I don't see any reason not to play with the expert game, so a full 7 is due.

RATING: 4
I'm not much of a co-op player, but this one tickles my thematic bone in the most delightful ways. This is perhaps the most thematically integrated rules set I've ever played. My firefighter friend's jaw dropped when he heard the terms I was throwing around to describe the game mechanics. Everything that occurs in the game is realistic (to the extent that any board game can realistically capture the elements of a fire and rescue situation). Like most co-ops (Space Alert and Hanabi being my only known exceptions), the caveat applies that if you have an optimizer in your group who is going to plan everyone's turns for them, this game will be a dud.

RATING: 7
Had a great time playing this making crude comments about the hosers, teammates flying out windows, and leaving victims on the sidewalk to get run over by the vehicles circling the building.  Yes, I am a horrible person.

The game however was not anything like horrible.  But like many co-op games, it was rather light and very crowd dependent.  Table-talk and anything that lower inhibitions while playing this game, such as sugar, sleep-deprivation, etc, are recommended.

It suffers less from the alpha-gamer phenomenon than some games, but I could see it as a possibility. 

The thrill of waiting to see if one teammate or another would get torched was quite fun.  Though I do wonder what kind of person it makes me when I start to take glee in watching a fictional firefighter get launched out a window into the side of the ambulance.  

I'll leave it at: mixed-feelings.  I don't see any other way to play it though other than with levity, a large group, at the highest difficulty, and with bad-jokes all around.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Um, yeah, I like cooperative games. I always thought that Pandemic was the poster child when it came to themes everyone should like. I mean who doesn't want to fight disease? But I think Flash Point has just taken Pandemic's spot in that respect. Fighting fires is such a cool theme. Rescuing lives should get everyone excited. I'm amazed how thematic the fire is despite the random placement. The way the heat slowly progresses from smoke, to fire, to explosions makes sense. The idea that fire next to smoke ignites that area as well, is just purely logical. So not only do you have a fun theme, but you have a theme that is tightly woven into the game's mechanisms. I found the different special roles and the related abilities to be nice and diverse. Plus the roles kind of influence how you want to play that character, so I could see a different game experience if I played with another character. I will say that there were a few of the minor rules, like the fire truck, which seemed a little too much. At a certain point it feels like one too many rules for a new player to follow, but you can ignore those aspects of the game and focus on your character's job. This might, with more play, actually elevate to the point of replacing Pandemic on my Top 10.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8
Several plays of the family version with my... well, with my family.  I've played this with my kids, ages 3, 6 and 9.  My 3 year old needed some help, but was doing a lot of things on his own.  My 6 and 8 year olds really had a lot of fun.  Most of the plays are coming down to the final few choices.

The "experienced" game is even better with more variation and requirements and special abilities.  As a family game, this is a definite winner!

So far, I'm pretty impressed with how this game works.  There are a lot of similarities between this and other recent co-ops (e.g. Pandemic), but it really plays out differently with a higher degree of randomness.  It's kind of what I'd expect fighting a fire to feel like.

RATING: 7
Reminded us strongly of Pandemic (though the addition of dice make it perhaps a touch more random and luck based). Move your firemen round the building, keeping the fire down and trying to rescue enough civilians before the building collapses. Didn't enjoy it quite as much as Pandemic for the additional randomness which can overpower good or bad play much more than in Pandemic and also because the roles are more restrictive. In Pandemic, the roles give additional abilities so everyone can cure diseases but the medic can do it better. In FP, however, your role pretty much precludes you from some things, so everyone can put out fires, one guy can do it better than the rest, but the two "rescue" guys can barely do it at all (double AP cost makes it prohibitively expensive). As a result, I felt I had fewer decisions open to me.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

Since it’s easy to explain and isn’t too difficult to play either, it can be a good choice as a gateway game.

RATING: 10
I've played many co-op games:  LOTR, Pandemic, Forbidden Island, Red November, Ghost Stories, and many more.  I feel like Flash Point might be the best co-operative game of them all -- at least the one I can recommend to the most people.  The theme is very real-world and approachable, and ties together with the intuitive game mechanisms very well.  And the game is very scalable in complexity, so it can be as simple as Forbidden Island or as challenging as Ghost Stories.  Players can even drop in and out fairly easily without messing the game up.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
I get a bit frustrated with this game, just because it's a classic Kickstarter job - good but unfinished. It has clever bits, but two core ideas - the hotspots and the roles - are really problematic. Too many of the roles (Hazmat Disposal, Imaging, Generalist) are lame and not that fun to play. The hotspots are frustrating because the game clearly needs them - the fire has to accelerate - but the mechanism itself is thematically vacuous in a game that otherwise pays fairly close attention to it's theme. Hotspots aren't hot, they aren't really more dangerous, the fire doesn't get worse there, they're just a die-roll trigger; it almost would have been better if they didn't have the "hotspot" thematic element.

I really wish this had been more developed. It's not bad, but it's weak in several areas that could easily have been overcome with some more development work.
---
Important Note: Make sure you're using a "good" d8. The one that came with the game doesn't work with the various rules sections that require you to "flip it over". It turns out that the heuristic we were using once we figured this out - making the faces should add up to 9 - is apparently wrong too. Either add or subtract 4, or the faces should add to 7 or 11. I am also suspicious of the quality of the die, we seem to get a lot of clustering.

Also, make sure you're playing the doors correctly - don't place two black cubes on a door that gets blown out, as the graphic design seems to indicate you should. If you do, the game will be impossible.
---
The basic/family game is very easy and fairly lame, but the "full" game is OK (I'd say don't even bother with the basic game, but the full game is complicated and fiddly enough and the basic game is short enough that I think it's worthwhile to start there). It's too random, and even with the hotspots it doesn't generate organic, escalating threat the way Forbidden Island, Pandemic, or Lord of the Rings do so well - it's much more of the "random stuff happens, do the best you can" than a game with real, well-managed tension. If you go after the fire aggressively early, you'll do fine, and there is an unfortunately high risk of the game being a boring cake-walk (if you roll "well") or impossible (if you roll poorly). But there is enough stuff going on in the full game to present tough choices from time to time. Unfortunately, all that stuff comes at a somewhat unreasonable cost in terms of rules and game complexity, so the bang for the buck is nowhere near as good as those three classics. Also, difficulty scaling with the number of players is a little uneven - large teams will have much more difficulty than small ones (this might be good; I enjoyed 5p more than 3p).

Also, too bad they couldn't include the "urban structures" in the base game (possibly by switching to card stock maps, or a paper overlay?). The slightly different difficulties and variations of the two included maps are quite helpful for giving the game a little more punch. I could see an additional pair of maps significantly increasing the replayability.

At the end of the day, a tough one to recommend. Vastly inferior to Pandemic, Forbidden Island, or Lord of the Rings. But it does play pretty quickly, and if you're burned out on those three or want a new coop in your rotation, not too bad.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7

RATING: 5
A decent intro-level cooperative game.  However, for games in this vein, I'd much rather play Pandemic as the game play here is both less interesting, and seems to have less tension.

The actions in the game are very basic, as you'll usually be either moving or fighting fire, and you may some times do things like chop through walls.  The goal is to find victims to drag to safety, so the game is about fighting enough fire in order to get everyone to safety.

Overall, an OK game, but there are better alternatives.

RATING: 7.5
Many of the core mechanics in this game (eg. use of action points, special abilities, the way the fire spreads) are derivative (see Pandemic), but they are so well integrated with the theme that this game is still distinct and worth playing.  The use of vehicles is neat, especially the ability to use the deck gun on the fire engine to put out fires.  I also like the flexibility that's required with regards to choosing your path into / out of the building, and the fact that you can chop through walls (causing structural damage at the same time) is very cool.  The game really does make one feel that one is wearing the boots of a firefighter.  I wish they had done a better job on the rulebook, though, and the player aids are poorly designed.

RATING: 5
Something of a provisional rating as I've played part of one game. Coop game decidedly in the mold of Pandemic. Shares a lot of the most appealing aspects of that game -- tension in spades, accessible rule set, relatively brisk running time. In fact, it bears enough of a resemblance (right down to the four actions per player, one special role per player, etc.) that I would be stunned if the designer didn't credit its forebear.

But comparisons can be insidious. Pandemic is very much a shared puzzle experience where the joy comes from collaborating on the best plan possible (within the scope of a sometimes-nebulous bit of half-information that comes from the fact that the game is driven by cards) and occasionally reaching into your stock of lateral thinking and realizing that the combination of my role PLUS her role PLUS this one event card we've been sitting on all game can flip a win to a loss in the last two turns IF Kinshasa isn't lurking on the top of the infection deck.

Flash Point isn't entirely NOT a puzzle, but what it really truly is a co-op tactical squad combat game -- a dungeon crawl with helpless fire victims in the place of the Amulet of Yendor and the Seven Keys of Vintoozler. You get in, you bash what you can, you loot, you scoot. It's a more visceral species of fun, one where the random elements sometimes bone you a way that Pandemic doesn't.

I don't know how much my reaction to this is colored by the fact that Pandemic was the first decent co-op game I've played and thus occupies a special place in my heart -- more than I'd like to admit, I'll wager -- but I do detect a distinct visceral vs. cerebral cleavage between the two games and my preference for Pandemic dovetails with my preference for the cerebral over the visceral.

That said, if your average co-op dungeon crawl was as well-designed as Flash Point was, I'd be a lot more interested in co-op dungeon crawls.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Co-op game with different difficulty levels that actually make a big difference (as opposed to Pandemic, which can be equally impossible with a bad card combo at the easiest difficulty level).

Although it is often quite easy to determine what is the best course of action, there will always be a lot of adjustment to changing circumstances.

Player turns are fast and all have an impact on the game, so nobody will have to be bored even in a six-player game. Being able to change roles during the game is great, as is chosing your own role (which is not officially allowed in Pandemic). It helps give the game a team feel, even when playing solo with two or more pawns.

The experienced game (difficulty levels 2, 3 and 4) does require a bit of thought at first, but the rules are logical enough to be memorised after a couple of games. The easiest difficulty suffers a bit from a lack of diversity in the long run, but is still a very enjoyable way to include casual players in the game.

The materials are all high-quality. My only criticism in this respect is that the back of the game board, which is also used, gets damaged very quickly at the folds. This is purely an esthetic issue though. The design of the board content is the very BEST part of the components, in my opinion, as it is very clear and informative.

I would highly recommend this game to anyone who loves co-op games. For those who feel even a burning home in a board game is bad, there is the consolation that you can at least chose to remove the dog AND the cat from the set of tokens used, so they at least will not be caught in the fire.

RATING: 6.5
This was a fantastic gift from my AU/NZ SS 2014.

My friends really like this game and one of my flatmates LOVES it. Since we all like playing games but I'm the only 'gamer' (i.e. I'm the only one who buys games), so it is great when you have other people requesting to play something.

One great thing about this game is how it has two sets of rules: the simplified game and the advanced game. This makes it easier to teach it to people - let them play the simplified version which isn't too complicated to learn, and then it isn't too difficult to teach them the rules of the advanced game. That's how we taught it to our friends and it seems to have served us well.

Another bonus: the double-sided board. Very clever to include this for added variety.

Update: My rating for this has slipped somewhat but it was a fantastic addition to my collection at the time. Nowadays I play with different people and this is a bit light for the group. However if you're looking for solid cooperative play other than Pandemic, this is a good choice.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Components: The boards are awesome (including in the expansion). Takes everything I love about floorplans and lets me run around in them putting out fires. The detail is great, and really enhances the theme. The firefighter figures in the second edition are very cool. The tokens are all top notch, and the art on the special roles cards looks great.

Experience: I didn't think too much of Pandemic while I was playing this game, which is to the game's credit. The theme absolutely works here. Fires are spreading left and right, we're finding all sorts of helpless people cowering beneath sinks and such, the walls are coming down, we're getting cut off from each other, there are explosions. Good stuff.

The special roles in the advanced game add some extra spice, and help to differentiate us from each other (e.g. I might forego putting out a nearby smoke, because it costs me more as the Rescue Specialist, but then later I regret it because that smoke turns to fire).

I've got to say, I definitely prefer this to Pandemic. Partly because I like the theme so much more. Pandemic is more abstract; just cube-covered dots connected by lines. But also because the choices are more difficult in Flash Point. In Pandemic, the uncertainty of the draw into player hands makes it more difficult to plan ahead, but when it's my turn, it usually seems pretty obvious what to do, with the only tough choice usually being between eradicating a disease and trying to prevent an outbreak. In Flash Point, my choices have less parity. Putting out smoke and fire is akin to removing cubes in Pandemic; but there's also the idea of discovering the identity of the trapped people, of deciding whether to break down walls; of protecting structural parts of the building; of closing a door behind me to prevent the spread of fire, or leaving it open for easier access. The geography of the floorplan is important, and I feel like I'm really having to coordinate with my teammates to make sure we are efficiently covering as much ground as possible.

My only real problem with the game, as with most cooperative games, is that the tension comes at us in the form of random events (the eruption of fire). I don't mind the puzzle aspect of this, but there is something missing when the game is merely throwing fire at us at random, rather than intelligently trying to outsmart us, trap us, cause explosions in vulnerable areas, etc. If we lose, I want it to be because we were outplayed, rather than because we didn't beat the odds. The only cooperative games I can think of that get around this issue are pre-programmed games (Sherlock Holmes Consulting Detective, Eagle Eye Agency), where the game is deliberately trying to mislead us.

First Played: 2011-11-29
Last Played: 2013-11-21
Plays (3):
4 players: 1
5 players: 1
6 players: 1

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
"AHHHH, it burns! Why does it hurt?!"
Why do these people have flammable cannisters just piled around their home? What is the cat doing on the stove? Why is there a black man trapped in the closet? Why are there so many people in such a small house? Who left a cigarette on the bed, and why won't it stay extinguished?!

I see a decent amount of parallels between this and Pandemic. However, I think I would always choose to play Pandemic over Flash Point. Mainly because I feel that Flash Point is more dependent on complete randomness when it comes to the dice-rolls for new fires and PoI's. Pandemic also has randomness for spreading the diseases, but it is controlled randomness that you can get a sense for -- you know that a location is either in the discard or still in the deck or has recently been shuffled back on top of the deck, or that a epidemic might occur soon and put the discard back on top. By comparison, in Flash Point, while unlikely it's entirely within the realm of possibilities to roll a never-ending series of explosive rolls; the dice mean that a game may be perfectly manageable because the fire spreads evenly and broadly, or a game is impossible because the fire keeps blowing up in the same places. In Pandemic, I feel like the CDC experts are predicting and trying to out-think the diseases and their spread. Flash Point also feels like firemen frantically trying to save people from a wild, uncontrollable fire; but I'd rather be out-thinking the destructive contagions than getting lucky with random nonsense blazes.

RATING: 6
Fun, if simple coop with lots of luck. The theme is great and works, but you feel you are at the mercy of the dice much of the time. Expansions make it more interesting.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.3
Cooperative game in which the players have to work together in order to fight fire in a house and save its inhabitants. Each round a player has 4 action points to spend. If you don't spend them all 4, you can save what's left for a future turn. After spending his or her action points the player throws 2 dice in order to determine where a new fire starts, or if it was already burning, where an explosion takes place (this can make holes in the walls and force closed doors to open or open doors to be permanently removed). As soon as an inhabitant is discovered a new point of attention (=inhabitant or fake) is also placed on the map by means of the same 2 dice.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
The theme in this game is so incredibly strong, even moreso than Pandemc, to which it is superficially similar.  The various maps offer different challenges, and the random spread of hazards combined with inherent dangers on the board are what build the constant tension that makes the game interesting.  The various character powers are distinct and all are interesting.  But the real innovation here is the ability of a player to swap out the character he's playing when the situation shifts to favor other special powers... but it takes precious time.

RATING: 9.5
Absolutely great game.  Excellent quality components, beautiful board, looks great when set up and being played.  We got a few really good cooperative games around the same time a few years ago (Forbidden Island, Pandemic, ...) and this is our favorite.  It oozes theme.  

We set it for medium difficulty and often the building collapses on our heads.  Great diversity of character roles.  Things happen somewhat randomly (where new fires pop up, etc.) but it is all about trying to control the situation.  Which means each player must utilize his character and work as a team.  If everyone makes a mad scramble to rescue victims, the whole crew is likely doomed.

Really great.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Let me start by saying, that even thought this is a relatively new game, and I'm probably still in the "honeymoon phase" of it, basking in the awesomeness of its newy glow, this is probably my second favorite coop game of all time. HOWEVER, its still not as fun at pandemic, and if you haven't played Pandemic: 1) Shame on you, you should run out and buy it NOW, 2) Disregard this review, because mostly I'm comparing them.

One question you might be asking yourself that I can answer is: Is Flashpoint just another Pandemic Clone like Forbbiden Island?" No, its not. They are both coop and have job cards and you move your pieces around a board, but thats pretty much where the similarity ends. For one thing, Flashpoint is much more random than Pandemic, which could be good or bad depending on what you like in a game. In flashpoint you roll dice to decide where new fires ignite. I think the mechanic for determining where viruses strike in Pandemic is better. Also, when you rescue survivors from the house, you HAVE to get them to the ambulance before a new event is rolled for. Which means, that you could walk into a room, grab a survivor, and then the next random roll puts another survivor right in the same room, What did you just step over then other guy last time you were in that room? In Pandemic you tend to move all over the board because the virus keeps spreading, but you don't find yourself returning to the same spot over and over and over like you do in Flashpoint. We actually decided that would be more fun is to have many different maps, with shorter games (ie, less victims to save, or maybe more victims on the maps as once (the game limit is 3). Also, and this is purely aesthetic, but I find the theme of Pandemic to be cooler than Flashpoint. I gave up wanting to be a fireman in about the 3rd grade, but it just so happens, that I am a scientist, so maybe I'm biased towards Pandemic for this reason.

Bottom line, Flashpoint is a great game, and in the coop gaming world, where there are less options, its currently one of the best, but its not THE BEST.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
[2 plays] This wasn’t extremely original—and maybe some of the coop games are starting to feel a little samey—but it was quite well done.  In this coop game, you're firefighters trying to rescue the inhabitants from a burning building.  

There are two levels of play, and I've only tried the basic level so far; we played once with the designated first-game setup, and once with the layout on the reverse side of the board.   I don't think you likely ever win this one in the sense of putting out the fire or saving the building.  Victory is defined as rescuing a certain number of people, and you have to balance your rescue efforts with your firefighting efforts; if you focus only on rescues and let the fire rage too far out of control, you may not be able to get to other victims, or the building may collapse (which means you lose).  

At the advanced level, there are Pandemic-style roles for the players; you become specialists in different skills.  This seemed like it would be fun, but require a bit more teamwork.  I would recommend playing the basic game first.  

One of the first things that struck me about this game was a sentence on the player aid that I can't recall ever seeing in a game before: you can SAVE leftover actions!  You have 4 actions per turn, and can bank up to 4 actions.  This is a really useful mechanic.  If you have one action left but need to do something that costs 2 actions, you don't lose the unused action, but can hoard it for later.  And having extra actions can let you successfully do things, like run into a room that's all ablaze and drag someone out, without standing there risking the flames.  

The production quality is excellent.  I think some things in the copy I played with were Kickstarter bonuses, though, like the wooden firefighter meeples.  But overall the quality is good and the design is clean.  The board comes with a different house on each side, and then there's a second board with a different building on each side.  That allows for a number of different scenarios.

Some of us found it mildly disturbing, on a thematic level, that saving the pets was just as important as saving the people.  Other than that, the only thing I disliked about this game was the fact that there are only three victims in the house at a time.  (When one is rescued or perishes, another is randomly generated.)  We played with 4 players, but I understand that even at the max of 6, there are only 3 victims.  Occasionally you feel like you don't have anything constructive to do because there aren't more people to rescue.  

On the whole, good game.  I would certainly play again, and look forward to the advanced level next time.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 8.5
Outstanding and terrifically themed Pandemic-style cooperative game where you team up to rescue victims from a burning house. 

See my pictorial review: http://www.boardgamegeek.com/thread/756411

[url=http://www.boardgamegeek.com/blogpost/3749/designer-diary-bringing-the-heat-to-flash-point-fi]Designer Diary[/url].  See also: [url=http://www.mediafire.com/?93km82o9tpd601p]java[/url] implementation of [url=http://www.boardgamegeek.com/thread/629392/a-great-pandemic-ish-co-op]original game[/url].

Ideas for adding elements of advanced rules gradually: 
- random setup of 3 explosions
- add vehicles (deck gun/driving makes game easier, ambulance requirement makes game harder)
- add specialists and hazmats/hotspots (specialists make game easier, hazmats/hotspots make game harder)

[url=http://www.boardgamegeek.com/article/8425530#8425530]FAQ on some rule questions[/url]

RATING: 9.5

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Feels like a grown up Pandemic. I appreciate what Pandemic brought in 2008, but this design has far more going on such that it totally and easily fires Pandemic. 

There's some nice lateral thinking in how you can run out to the fire truck and change roles, get something done, then go change again. Like change into a dog, pull some victims out, then change into a firefighter and spray some fires. The ambulance and fire truck add nice peripheral decisions for the actions of your characters. For example, you have to load the victims into the ambulance, not just pull them out of the fire, so you want to move it to where you plan on exiting. Touches like this feel like they were quite smartly incorporated and not tacked on.

Lastly, the different maps and scenarios are a huge improvement. It's much more fun to have different maps to play each time instead of the same one over and over.

All in all, I'm impressed. It's still a light game that relies on the old school design of co-contribution more than cooperation and can lend itself to Alpha Player Syndrome, but there's enough going on here to make it worth the occasional play for me.

RATING: 7.5
I like this game a lot and find everyone I introduce it to like it as well.  It is very easy to explain because the actions you can take are very intuitive.  This game is great for new gamer (or non-gamers) because what you should do on your turn is intuitive (hey there is fire beside me, I think I should put it out).  Even if it is not the optimal play your new players will feel like they are contributing and they will be able to make the decisions themselves.  Additionally, the roles in the game do assist players to narrow down what options they would want to do on a turn (some players will specialize in fire, other is saving victims), so that reduces thinking time between turns.

I do find this great for more advanced players as well because you do have to plan ahead and there are harder maps.  The fire is random, so it keeps you on your toes and makes the game different every time.

RATING: 8
I had avoided Flash Point for a long time, thinking that it may just be a slightly more family-friendly clone of Pandemic. But I was pleased to learn that it while it has some similarities, it's really its own game with its own feel.  My children were totally immersed in the theme of this game, and felt like firefighters with different jobs doing their best to save lives.  I think Pandemic is a little more gamerly and feels a little less random, but Flash Point is not all random either.  I think it's every bit as tough to win as Pandemic and in the end, I like it just a little more. The integration of the theme is superb with the tense anticipation of watching the fire spread, and the desperation of seeing the building start to collapse around you.

RATING: 10
This game is fab, I love it. Co-op games are my favorites, and the theme of this one is unique and deep, and the hilarity of constantly spawning victims to save, often repeatedly in the same room, makes the storytelling aspect very fun as well. "Now, where did Muscle Tee come from? Under the sink? Was he hiding there waiting for Professional Suit to leave for work so he could continue his affair with Redhead?" My friend (who owns the game, and most of our games) and I call this game "Crispy Cat" or some variation, as our failures have tended to hinge on the destruction of the crucial kitty cat victim. Cats and dogs are just as important as humans! It's also hilarious to us that the female firefighters are all dolled up; never look less than your best, even in the middle of a raging fire!

RATING: 5
The first few play throughs, this game is very exciting and fun, but as you play more, you begin to see the repetitive nature of this game. Roles begin to be divided between just firefighting and civilian rescue and this gets quite old after a while, but it seems to be the best way to win the game by far. The mechanics behind how the fire spreads is a pretty exciting part of the game and it can make the game pretty challenging; one of its high points. I find myself, however, never wanting to play this game just because the strategy of the roles is not complex enough for me.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 4
I have a somewhat strange relationship with Flash Point. It's a game I can't really fault much on its gameplay or its components, and yet it fails on all levels at delivering a compelling experience. First of all, I find the theme terribly boring. I must confess I didn't buy the game. It was offered to me. If I look past that, the game design works well for the most part, and yet its entertainment value is very low. Once you figure to focus all your efforts on containing the fire first and only then rescuing victims, playing always feels more or less the same. If you think of the situation it depicts, you should feel tension and excitement as you play, but they're largely absent. As for the art, it falls into the same pitfall. Map and cards and counters are properly done, they're not ugly, but they don't have more personality that a collection of clip arts. If I look at the games in my collection, plenty are more flawed than Flash Point, and yet it is the last one I'll pick up. It's quick to set up, the rules are simple and effective, but it feels like a chore to play, and this is hard to forgive. In the end, Flash point is so uninspired that it just fails to inspire.

RATING: 8

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
The most obvious comparison for Flash Point is the game Pandemic. The two games are very similar in style, weight, and length. My experience has been that the decisions and tactics are much easier and more straightforward in Flash Point. For this reason, I prefer Pandemic, although I would recommend either game to fans of cooperative play. Those who prefer a game with a very concrete, realistic, and vivid approach to its theme may favor Flash Point. Flash Point gets an A+ for theme, whereas Pandemic feels more abstract and game-y.

The other element that leads me to prefer Pandemic over Flash Point has to do with the way that the two games handle randomness. Pandemic uses cards, which gives it two advantages over the dice that are used in Flash Point. First of all, the card-based system of Pandemic allows for the diseases to strike the same locations repeatedly. The epidemic cards are so deadly because of the way that they stack the top of the deck. That just wouldn't be possible with dice. Secondly, all of the dice rolling in Flash Point gets to be a nuisance. The turn-to-turn upkeep is more fatiguing, and a lot of that has to do with the dice.

Finally, I really really really really hate the graphic design of Flash Point. The character cards are nicely done, but everything else looks like it was designed by a colorblind person. The board is way too busy and the colors are way too saturated.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9
This game has so much of what we love. Cooperative strategy, options for difficulty and mechanics, an immersive theme, and various boards with the expansions to keep game play fresh and adapt to different comfort levels with gaming and/or different desires in terms of weight and game length.

I also found that the game negates "bored when it isn't my turn" because constant communication is imperative to keeping on top of the ever-changing board. Stop to read emails while other people did their thing? You missed three explosions, a rescue, and the collapse of a wall and now you're trapped and need to bust down a wall to get out. I also didn't find that quarterbacking was an issue, mostly because after every play turn the fire evolves and plans can't usually be made in advance. It's very much a react and hold your butts kind of game.

We loved it so much that we immediately played three more times and then had to force ourselves to play something else.

This is the ideal game for our household.

RATING: 8
Even with just the beginner rules this game is fun. It has a good rollercoaster of excitement going as the fire starts and is put out that keeps each play unique. Feels very rewarding to play. With the advanced rules this turns nail-biting very quickly. It still feels very fluid with the additional rules/roles and keeps itself rewarding. Expansions are all excellent. Heroic difficulty is a serious challenge, still haven't beaten it yet. Game has a bit of a nice decrescendo to it once the fire is under control.

Sometimes the game seems overly difficult as a result of poor rolls, but in these situations we tend to just restart the scenario or laugh at how screwed we are.

Have Dangerous Waters, Extreme Danger, Honor and Duty, Fire Dog and Veteran, Tragic Events.

RATING: 7
A much better game than Pandemic where you don't have much freedom of choice.
In this game, you get to choose where you start, where you go and what you should do, whether in basic or advance game, unlike pandemic where the game tells you "where to go" each turn.
Your play is not dictated by the game, even if you are still not in control of much like in Pandemic. You still are free to go wherever you like, pretty much like in Arkham Horror where you are pressed in time, but still can do whatever you like.

RATING: 9.8
Pandemic is my favorite game. I have logged around 75 plays since picking it up back in 2013. I am not sure why it took me so long to get this one on  the table. Perhaps because I had a bad experience with Defenders of the Realm and the dice scared me away. Anyway, I just started playing it last month and have already logged 21 plays with the base game. What makes it so unique? For me it is the pace of the game. It is not as much of a brain burning puzzle as Pandemic, but running around, putting out fires, and saving people is just exciting. I have had a few games ruined by dice rolls, but that is certainly the exception rather than the rule. I play on the back of the board (harder side) typically on veteran with 4 random characters. With that my win pct is right around 60 or 70% which for me is the sweet spot, it is a very well balanced game that scales well with different player counts and difficulty levels. I have played about 10 heroic games on the back side as well, pulling out wins in 3 of them. I am not sure I like it that hard though, many of the losses I never even had a chance to win. Will it replace Pandemic? Never. It provides a great alternative. I can play 2 games in the same amount of time and the experience is similar enough they are comparable, but different enough that I feel they have managed to completely differentiate themselves.

RATING: 7

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 3
(05/18/2012) Comment based on one play.

This is yet another cooperative where random crap happens, and it is a desperate race to accomplish some task before the game kills you. Perfect fodder for alpha-males, which is the bane of most cooperatives.

While it is based on a solid theme about firefighting--you can swear the theme from "Backdraft" is playing in the background--the mechanics are somewhat bland. Admittedly, play is simple and straightforward, based on an action point menu, and each player in control of a firefighter with unique abilities. While there is very little downtime, I was left with the feeling that I had no control over the outcome. Fires sprung up here and there, based on dice rolls, and if we were unlucky--which was most of the time--explosions occurred, structural integrity of the building suffered, and victims were killed. Exciting for those who enjoy plenty of randomness and chaos. I'll steer clear of this in the future. I rate it a '3', with room to drop.

On a side note, this is yet another data point for me to stay away from Kickstarter games. Most Kickstarter games seem to be lacking in game development or polish, having not gone through the traditional vetting process. If one is successful in generating a lot of buzz, it is possible for many mediocre and relatively unsophisticated titles (compared to today's state of the art) to be published. Buyer beware.

Advanced rules add a lot more depth and introduced new mechanics that take this from 'light' to 'light-medium'.  Luck of dice rolls and strategy go hand-in-hand.  Nice board, thick cardboard chits, and plastic cubes make for average components. Double sided board with a few expansions (not included) and with solo rules make this highly replayable and quick..say..30 minutes.

RATING: 5
Flash Point has a great theme and is very friendly to new gamers, but as someone who has played quite a few games and co-ops, I find it falls flat. This is mostly due the random dice rolls that dictate how the fire spreads (the game's chief obstacle). More strategic co-op games tend to provide information about what might be coming up next. This one can't and the result is a wildly varying play experience: sometimes it's a walk in the park and sometimes it is near impossible, even on the same difficulty level.

For me, there are too many good co-op games (including the similar but more enjoyable Pandemic) to spend time on Flash Point.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
A nice cooperative game with a strong firefighting theme.  Getting the fire under control is no guarantee, because you can think everything is just fine when suddenly fire sweeps through the building.  By the same token, a house seemingly filled with fire is not a guaranteed loss.

The biggest complaint I have is that the rulebook is not as clear as it could/should be, especially for players that jump to the "experienced" game right away.  The experienced game is not so complicated that a group of experienced gamers needs the training wheels of the basic game.  But the experienced rules are written as "just like the basic game, except...."  We have to constantly flip back and forth for, "What is the basic rule, what is the exception."  So setup is difficult and figuring out the ongoing gameplay is worse.  Since I don't play every day or every week, I don't remember all the rules between plays, nor do the (changing cast of) people I play with.  As a result, I'm not sure I've yet played with all the correct rules all at once.  There's still lots of "Wait, we forgot..." and "Oh yeah, we should have...."

RATING: 6
Very fiddly compared to even Pandemic. Not so much as in the number of components which there are a lot, but many different kinds of components to keep track of at one time.  A lot of rules you have to remember compared to Pandemic or Forbidden Island.  Don't understand how people say it's easier to learn than Pandemic...sheesh.

Theme is great.  It just hurts may head trying to manage this game.  My kids love it though.

There are some rules that don't make sense and are hard to remember like placing the POI marker in the "Experienced" game.  

I prefer Pandemic, Forbidden Island, and Castle Panic over this.

RATING: 2.5
2013-04-17

Initial Rating: 3.0 (April 2013)

VERY boring game, I wasn’t expecting a good game and I wasn’t disappointed :S. This is worse than Pandemic (another game I don´t like), I had zero fun playing this and I hope to never play it again. 

Now to my reasons. The theme doesn’t do anything for me (although I recognize it is a novel theme) so I don’t care about it one way or another. With 4 players I felt the down time to be excessive, I shudder to think how the game will play with 5 or more players. I tend to play quickly so I did and it took “decades” for my turn to come back. The decisions are obvious 99% of the time, it is completely random where the fire will spread, if you roll well you will win, if you roll poorly you will lose, lots of chaos, zero strategy.

I liked the variety of roles and the fact that you can change them in the game, however I feel they are unbalanced (for example The Driver). Playing with him you have to always do the same actions throughout all the game, very boring. The game components are very well done, it`s just that the gameplay sucks. 

Bottom line Flash Point can be fun to some people, but not for me. I will do my best to stay away from this game. If I want to play a Co Op game, I would play Space Alert, Hanabi, Sentinels for the Multiverse or Arkham Horror over this one. 

Current Rating: 2.5

RATING: 6
As a Firefighter I love seeing a pretty cool simulation come out. It's far from perfect but at least it's SOMETHING! I would quibble about each player being an all in one Firefighter as Pumpermen don't carry axes, they carry and lighten-up the hose. Laddermen carry ventilation tools and this part is totally left out of the game and it's vitally important in a real fire. The Ladder Pipe wouldn't be used until the building was lost so that's off too. Last but not least the "Rescue Specialist" is a lady with makeup on!!! She should have been on the "Imaging Tech" card. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8.5
This is one of my go-to gateway games. I have used it to introduce many people to the world of nerdy gaming and they always want to play again. Heck, even my wife -- who is not a gamer -- has introduced this to new players of her own volition in my absence! There's something in the premise of being a team of firefighters that people latch onto easily. I love how quickly they get emotionally attached to each of the victims (faceless, generic, slightly people-shaped pictures on blue tokens) so that it comes off as genuinely sad if anyone is killed.

Positives: Very simple mechanics. My 4-year-old daughter can happily play the family game! Anyone can be comfortable with their options on their turn within 15 minutes of starting. Strategy, on the other hand, comes with experience. You only need to play the family game once to be able to play with the far superior and not much more complicated advanced rules. It gets genuinely tense and there's a real sense of urgency once the fire starts to spread near PoIs.

Negatives: As with all co-ops, it can be very easy for one player to dominate the others' turns. Waiting between turns can drag on a bit, especially if you're playing with more than 4, a couple of new players, or someone who suffers from AP. The fire engine is useless without the crew chief and only works haphazardly with him.

RATING: 3
Why not play Pandemic instead... this is not different enough. I cannot give this game a rating higher than I give Pandemic because it has the same weakness: the game can be reduced to solitaire play. There is no point playing this game with more than 1 player as they contribute nothing to the game play mechanics. A good coop game needs something that truly requires teamwork: traitor role, real-time or hidden information. This game has none of them, just like Pandemic. The whole "pure coop" genre is flawed and much less interesting than other coop genres. If you like that kind of games, you may want to check this out. Otherwise, this brings nothing new to the table.

RATING: 8
I'd want to play it again, but it strikes me as a nice variant on Pandemic. I like the theme better, and I feel like the game is working against me less. To clarify, in Pandamic, the deck is very limited and it's easy to loose because the deck runs out, and there's no way to stop it. In Flash Point, there are also timing mechanism (e.g. damage to house), but choices can be made which prolong or shorten the timing. 

I also like being able to fully see the board situation in Flash Point (as opposed to Pandemic which heavily encourages remembering which cities are in play / have been played). The games are very similar, but I like the sense of control/direction that Flash Point offers, even if the house is burning down around you.

RATING: 9
An incredible game, with varying levels of complexity and difficulty.  It's a lot like Pandemic, except that for me, the global disease theme in Pandemic is too big, and that makes it seem more distant and less aligned with the cooperative mechanic.  By contrast, the setting and mission in Fire Rescue are far more intimate - a single dwelling, with people trapped inside.  It gives the game more emotional punch.  If you like cooperative games, this is a must-own.

Now, that being said, I've seen games play out really differently based on dice rolls.  Some games have been a breeze, the fire under control, and the people and even small animals quickly moved to safety.  Other games have been overwhelming hellfire pits from which no firefighter was ever going to emerge alive.  And other games seem to be going well until a few poor decisions combine with a few unlucky dice rolls and the building collapses on your head.  Some folks might find this to be too random, but it works just fine for me.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: N/A
Flash Point: Fire Rescue is a cooperative game of fire rescue. In both variants, players are attempting to rescue 7 of 10 victims from a raging building fire.
 As the players attempt to rescue the victims, the fire spreads to other parts of the building, causing structural damage and possibly blocking off pathways through the building. Each turn a player may spend action points to try to extinguish fires, move through the building, move victims out of the building or perform various special actions such as moving emergency vehicles. If 4 victims perish in the blaze or the building collapses from taking too much structural damage, the players lose. Otherwise, the players win instantly when they rescue a 7th victim.

RATING: 7
[u]Comments:[/u]
Over the years I have come to appreciate cooperative games more and more. I enjoy them for the team building, the puzzle solving, and the overall different experience they treat their players with than a competitive game does. Flash Point is a decent entry into this world offering the players a theme that is almost tailored made for the genre, fighting fires in various locations. Each player plays as a different type of firefighter with different abilities that will help them and hinder them throughout the game. In another perfect match the fire spreads in completely random ways through the roll of a dice. The mechanics are pretty solid throughout the game. The player abilities make each character feel unique, although that does tend to lock each player into doing one specific thing during a fire (but I am guessing that is pretty thematic anyway). What I really had an object too was that this, even more so than most cooperative games, didn't really offer very meaningful choices. it was pretty obvious what you should do on a turn and if you deviated from that the whole group definitely suffered quite a bit. I didn't feel like I had anything I could do other than what I was expected to do. The game can be quite tense and that is a lot of fun, and it is most definitely a challenge, but overall I am glad i played someone else's copy and didn't buy this myself. I much prefer other co-op games. 
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 9
I've been a big fan of [thing=30549][/thing], so when I saw [thing=100901][/thing] I was pretty interested.  We had missed the Kickstarter campaign, but we ended up preordering the game.

The components are very nice and the gameplay feels intuitive and fluid.  The game is a little more random than Pandemic, but I found that this fit the theme better and actually made the game more tense---you never know where a blaze is going to go up.  Plus, I think the random nature makes the game less deterministic and less prone to easy decisions and one player dictating everyone's actions.  Each role is significantly more different from each other than in Pandemic, which fits the teamplay better.  The game also felt more personal, bringing the threat from the global scale of Pandemic to the family scale.  It even has a dog and cat that you can rescue!

On the other hand, my wife wasn't a huge fan of this with just two.  I do think that most cooperative games work better with more people, as you get more a team play aspect to it.  Still, this is much better to solo play than Pandemic, so I've gotten several plays in with just myself.  
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
My favorite coop, as of this writing.  Has a large amount of theme compared to other coops.  And this is the only game that I have ever played where, after the game has been won, people want to keep playing it anyways...because we have to rescue these totally real people from the burning building!

I like the player powers.  They really do differentiate what the players can do.  And I like that you're not even locked in to keep your character if you figure it the situation really calls for a different one.

I like the easy version compared to the advanced version.  It's just a lot easier to teach and get people into it.  And I still enjoy the easy version quite a bit.  

The only problem with the game is the randomness.  Based on where the fires come out the game could be a lot harder or a lot easier.  How far do you have to go to get to the fires?  How many explosions are there?  Does it keep building up in an area and knock out a bunch of walls?  Does the fire happen to land next to a victim?

Fortunately, the advanced version helps you mitigate a lot of the unlucky things because of the player powers and the firetruck.  If one place gets out of hand with fire you can address that better than in the simple version.  So I think that really helps.  And furthermore, the randomness doesn't bother me because that feels realistic, and what this game does so well is making you feel engaged with a realistic theme.

The only thing that's not so thematic is the way that new points of interest pop up.  You could rescue six people from the same small room.  Really?  You somehow didn't see them the first four times you were in the room?  But we get over that pretty easily.

I love this game because it feels like you are doing something that matters in real life.  That is markedly absent from most games.  It's just a fresh idea.

Furthermore, quarterbacking doesn't seem to be much of a problem with this one.  Not that you couldn't, but, there are usually options.  It's pretty easy to, as the experienced player, lay out some options, and show the pros and cons of both, while emphasizing the cons of the worst option, and let the person decide. 

Which brings me to my next point: meaningful decisions.  The game usually gives you a meaningful decision every turn.  Maybe multiple.  And because the turns are so fast, and the fire is constantly developing, player engagement is high.

I really like the components.  Love the black cubes.  It was very good that they made it a double-sided board.  I hope I can buy more boards for it eventually.  The only downside I can see really is that some people will be annoyed at the really small "hot spot" tokens.

Really glad they used miniatures for the player tokens.  Really glad they didn't make the box oversized.  There are a lot of tokens; I put a small plano box in there to hold them, which majorly helps speed up setup/tear-down.

Overall I don't have any major complaints.  Maybe if I play it a bunch more and decide it is too random after all that could lower it, but I think that probably won't happen.

Love it!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5.5
One of the things that sucks about a lot of co-ops is that as individual player, you feel a bit helpless to impact the outcome of the game... winning comes by working together, which means you really have to share your thoughts and strategy and discuss them with other players. Flash Point does this too. There are lots of fiddly special-case rules, which are especially bad in co-ops since there is an advantage to overlooking them (and no incentive for other players to spot them). Play is lots of thinking and weighing of options, but very little actual action. Randomness and bad-luck feel like they have as much impact on the outcome as any actual strategy. Yuck.

Look, I get that there are people who love co-ops because they're non-confrontational, or because they can be played solo or with people who lack the will and/or capacity to learn the rules properly, and that's just great. Those sorts of people will probably get good use out of a game like Flash Point. For me, a co-op needs to be a bit more special. Putting out fires is a novel theme, but I much prefer exploring the world in Eldritch Horror.

RATING: 6
(Review after owning game for 4+ years):

For a game that is a board game version of playing with firetrucks and living out every childhood dream, it is fairly complicated and difficult to play. Gaming elements (rolling for fire, progressing fire, moving trucks) have just a bit too much abstraction so that they distract from the thematic elements of being a team of heroic firefighters. With the right group there are times of triumph with somewhat hysterical elements, such as being stuck in a burning bathroom while carrying the house cat. But these are few an far between. I haven't finished a game without the feeling of doing chores, so I wouldn't recommend this one.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I like this game as well as Pandemic. I love cooperative games in general. I liked the simplicity of Pandemic, but in two expansions, it become more complex to play and teach, thus not ideal as a gateway game if you try to include everything. Flash Point offers expansions, but complexity is not as swift as with Pandemic. It's still there though. With Flash Point: I particularly like the idea of saving actions, because it seems very thematic not to rush into a fire just to use all of your action points. The opportunity to change roles midgame is inspired as well. I ordered expansions after our first play, but tried to stick with maps and characters over new and exciting (dangerous) rule additions. I think Flash Point may become our coop gateway of choice and we will be playing this with our grandson at the earliest opportunity. Excellent and highly recommended.

RATING: 7
Gefällt mir ganz gut, das Spiel hat aber ein Problem, dass mit nach mehr Partien immer stärker auffällt: Die Partien können zu unterschiedlich verlaufen, was den Schwierigkeitsgrad betrifft. Wenn man "Glück" hat, fallen die Würfel so, dass es herausfordernd aber nicht unfair ist. Dann macht das Spiel wirklich Spaß und würde von mir sogar 8 Punkte erhalten. Es kann aber auch anders laufen...
Auf ein und der selben Schwierigkeit kann man chancenlos untergehen oder relativ problemlos gewinnen. Es kann sich ein fast erloschenes Feuer (also fast keine Feuer/Rauch-Marker mehr auf dem Brett) durch unglückliche Würfelwürfe innerhalb von 2-3 Spielerzügen in ein nicht kontrollierbares Flammendes Inferno (insofern passender Untertitel) verwandeln, wo man plötzlich, obwohl alles gut aussah, chancenlos verliert, so mehrmals bei meinen ca. 20 Partien passiert. Da man anders als z.B. in Pandemie oder die vergessene Stadt keinerlei Hinweis darauf hat, wo das Übel (hier in Form des Feuers) auftritt, so dass man aufgrund von statistischen Überlegungen abschätzen könnte, wo es wichtiger wäre zu handeln, wirkt dies nur frustrierend, weil man sich nichtmal denken kann "ah ja, dass hätten wir vielleicht so besser machen können", sondern einfach nur dasitzt und sich denkt: "Mhh, war bei dem Würfelpech halt nicht zu gewinnen, schade..."
Ich habe an und für sich überhaupt nichts gegen Glück in einem kooperativen Spiel, aber es sollte entweder einschätzbar sein oder ausgleichende Mechanismen geben, so dass Extreme nur sehr selten sind. Hier ist das Gegenteil der Fall: Wenn man Pech hat und viele Explosionen hintereinander würfelt, erhöht dies die Chance weitere Explosionen zu würfeln. Da man selber keinerlei Einfluss darauf hat diesen Teufelskreis zu durchbrechen (da man keine Möglichkeit hat abzuschätzen, wo es wichtiger ist das Feuer zu löschen), ist das Spiel in dieser Hinsicht unausgegoren.
Dadurch haben einige Partien einen sehr faden Beigeschmack und zeigen, dass es dem Spiel an einem Mechanismus fehlt, der die Schwierigkeit balanciert. Umgekehrt, wenn man was das Feuer betrifft Glück hat, kann man sich alle Zeit der Welt lassen die Leute einen nach dem andern aus dem Haus zu holen, während die anderen Spieler das aufkeimende Feuer in Schach halten. Da es keinen Timing-Mechanismus (wie z.B. in Pandemie, Die Zwerge oder Eldritch Horror) gibt, der einen zwingt in einer bestimmten Zeit fertig zu werden. Dies sorgt dann für relativ langweilige Partien, in denen nach der Anfangsphase nie echte Gefahr besteht.
Bisher waren für mein Gefühl etwas mehr als die Hälfte der Partien gut von der Balance, der Rest entweder zu einfach oder "ungewinnbar" aufgrund der Würfel. Eigentlich eine zu geringe Quote, trotzdem mag ich das Spiel mehr, als ich erklären kann, da es wie aufgeführt einige gravierende Mängel im Spieldesign besitzt, und gebe ihm dennoch 7 Punkte.

RATING: 5
This is a beautifully produced, well-themed, carefully thought-out game that leaves me flat. It's close to Pandemic in so many ways that it's hard not to compare the two, and Flash Point lacks the spark of Pandemic for me. I don't see a compelling reason to own both.

With Pandemic, my very first game made me want to play again on the spot; that didn't happen with FP. It's a good game, but competing against a stable of co-ops that I love to play and rate more highly (Pandemic 10, Defenders of the Realm 9, Elder Sign 9, and Yggdrasil 8), it needed to bring something special to the table.

My group felt pretty much the same way: fun game, but less fun than alternatives we already have on hand. And I feel sort of bad about that -- FP really is an excellent game, and one that a lot of folks will enjoy a great deal.

After it went several months with no plays beyond the first, I sold it.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
The beginner's rules are just to learn, go for the advanced rules to have serious fun.

The enemy is the fire, and it behaves quite randomly, which is consistent with the theme. Tension really builds up as the fire proceeds and accelerates, threatening the people and pets in the house with death.

Teamwork is essential to take advantage of the specialised skills of the firefighters. Actually, you'll end up feeling that the individuality of each player gets fuzzier and fuzzier until everybody discusses everybody else's moves.

Even with mostly cardboard parts, the aesthetics of the game is satisfactory and the fire spreading through dice cast with explosions and crumbling walls gives a creepy pleasure also in matches that end in a defeat.

My personal approval for making a game about heroism based on the value of life, work and co-operation. Enough with war, trade and deception!

RATING: 7
Flash Point: Fire Rescue is a co-operative game in which players take on the roll of firefighters.  Each firefighter has unique skills that will need to be used to best advantage in order to fight back flames, seek out and eliminate hazardous materials, and locate and save residents of a burning house.

The pressure is on immediately as the fire spreads unpredictably.  It's not easy finding the people inside either.  Sometimes when you suspect there's someone in a room you find out the intelligence is faulty when you get there.  If you can save at least 7 people before the flames, and explosions, kill them, or destroy the house, then players win!  Good luck.

Flash Point: Fire Rescue is a fun game that is just soaked with theme.  It draws players in immediately.  Right from the beginning you're thinking about how you're going to get the fire under control, quickly get in, grab the people inside, and get out.

If you like co-ops, intense game play, or just well done games, then I highly recommend this one!

RATING: 7
This is a great co-op game. The rules are a little fiddly for complete non-gamers to pick up without a gamer to help them through it (those hot spots, flash overs and explosions are not so well explained). It's more complex than Forbidden Island, but less gamerly than Pandemic. The replayability comes from the random location of the PoIs and the randomness of the fire spreading mechanism, but that doesn't seem to matter. Now that there are two (soon to be three) expansions, each providing a different set of rooms to work in, there is a lot to explore. Added to that there are difficulty levels (the higher levels are HARD). Lots of fun in the light/short game category
