=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
Flash Point or D-Day Dice?

Everyone seems to compare this game to Pandemic. I get why - both have increasing dangers to be controlled and both are co-ops. But Pandemic sucks. No seriously, it does, you just haven’t noticed. 

A more interesting comparison is to D-Day Dice. The goal is different (movement vs control) but both are co-ops, and fun. Also, both are similar in board design and components. Both are also a little easy (DDD broken with Lieutenant, see threads there). More important, both offer a wide variety of scenarios and replayability. But to that, it seems DDD gives you more bang for your buck. 

Also, FP seems a little more random. Not only because there are dice (I like dice btw), but because that drives where things show up. DDD is more linear there. So I guess it’s interesting to go in, knock down some walls, save a couple people, go out – then rinse and repeat. But either it’s easy because you have a path, or it’s frustrating because it’s too random. I think some of the expansions help here though, but there you have to pay more to get to that. 

I’m certainly glad for the Kickstarter success for FP, but I’m underwhelmed since it’s still just a solo game. All co-ops are solo. Even if you work around the Dominant Personality Problem, you are still inherently left with 2 problems: the DP *wants* to tell the “idiot” what to do and so is frustrated; the “idiot” knows they’re the idiot, and so the game isn’t as fun.  All good for a learning game I suppose, but after that?

At least neither DDD or FP suffer the Arkham Horror travesty of lasting 3+ hours (or 30 min if you die early). Minor point: Space Alert is actually playable solo with multiple “players” and increasing difficulty as there is enough time to map out all the ladder logic required to win. However, it is actually fun with a group since people will react differently and the time pressure is there. Perhaps AH would benefit from a timer?

If you can get it for cheap, or like solo games, it is well done – go for it.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6.5
Game in a Nutshell: Co-op game of saving people from a burning building.

Played as: 3 player

Pros: Great theme that is very apparent through the game. You almost start to feel warmer upon entering a room full of fire. The game can be scaled both in difficulty and complexity making it easy to play with a range of temperaments and abilities.

Cons: It doesn't break the mold of cooperative games where it feels like a group optimization puzzle and suffers from all the usual pitfalls because of it. No one wants a "bossy" player, but it's not fair that the bossy player should feel like they need to disengage in order to hold back.

Other: I played as a convention demo and was taught by a very tired demoer. We started playing MANY things wrong, and tried to right the ship as we went along. Things definitely improved as we went, but I need to admit that there's a good chance we still haven't got a proper full game experience (though I'm comfortable with the comments I've made thus far).

Best Use: Has that go-to quality for an introductory cooperative game.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Despite running into some complications with misunderstood rules (and consequently thought at the time that the game was much more difficult than it actually is), this is an excellent game! Only played with the family rules so far, so we haven't yet seen everything this game has to offer. Definitely one of the best releases of 2011 in my opinion, and well worth the wait. With any luck the harder difficulties will present a healthy challenge.

I'm also quite pleased that this offers a considerably different experience to Pandemic. Not to say I dislike Pandemic (in fact, I love it), but if this game managed to outshine Pandemic with similar, superior gameplay, Pandemic would undoubtedly remain permanently shelved, and thus a waste of money.

However, while Pandemic offers more in strategy, Flash Point: Fire Rescue excels in its tactical gameplay. With Pandemic, it is possible to plan ahead: as players can gain a general understanding of what is to come, and therefore plan in advance to tackle the issues. With Flash Point: Fire Rescue, the chaotic nature of the fire means that long term strategies, while possible, can fall to pieces. Thus, it is best to assess the immediate and short-term future and work tactically, rather than working out a master plan. 

Thematically, the strategic nature of Pandemic and the tactical nature of Flash Point are perfect for their respective titles. Flash Point contains exciting gameplay, and the fire in this game never feels like a puzzle to solve (a quirk frequently mentioned of Pandemic) as it's random, fluid nature and the way it interacts with the deteriorating building structure means a player can never truly "solve" this game.

Ultimately, this game deserves the backing it received on Kickstarter, and deserves the praise it garners. If you're wondering whether Pandemic or Flash Point is the better title to buy, however, my answer is that you should definitely buy both. Flash Point contains rules that have clearly derived from Pandemic, but is certainly not a Pandemic clone; and both offer a truly unique, enjoyable game experience. If you enjoy one of these titles however do not own the other, definitely do yourself a favour and grab a copy of the other. You'd be hard pressed not to enjoy them both.

RATING: 6
I like the theme. I like the tension. But the game gets very repetitive for me. Extinguish fire. It flares up. Extinguish it again. It flares up again. Pick up a victim. Oops, false alarm. Go back and extinguish smoke. Move to new victim. Smoke flares up. Smoke explodes. Use the truck. Extinguish. It explodes again. Use the truck again. Move to victim. Smoke again. Get victim, move a spot. Douse the smoke. Move a spot. 

In all of these situations, are you rolling dice between each turn, often times multiple times. To win, you need 7 victims rescued. This can easily take 90 minutes or more, which is too long for the gameplay offered.

I really like this theme. I want it to be cleaned up, and create a 30 minute hair-raising, pulse-pounding, scenario that leaves you wanting more.

RATING: 7
[microbadge=1714]

[u]16-Jan-2013[/u]:  This is an excellent family/cooperative game where you take on the roles of firefighters trying to rescue people from a burning building.  The theme is the big draw with this one.  You really get the sense of rushing into danger and trying to get potential victims out of harm's way.

I had to bring up a comparison to Pandemic, but everyone seems to so...this is similar to that game in terms of the different roles, the cooperative play, and the intensity.  However, Flashpoint is much more random than Pandemic.  You use two dice to determine what the fire (the enemy) will do during the game.  Sometimes it's just a little smoke, sometimes it turns into a series of explosions creating havoc.  But this is also where the fun comes in.  You just never know what the flames will do from turn to turn.

I picked up the two expansions as well as I like variety in my games.  All together there are six different locations, some of them adding in new mechanisms and even one new role.  If you enjoy this game, these are an easy buy in my opinion.  I'm still learning the new maps, but again, the variety is awesome.

[u]24-Jan-2014[/u]:  We have really had a lot of fun with this one over the past year.  It's my youngest daughter's favorite game, perhaps?  Definitely up there in her top 3.  I recently rediscovered the fun with playing this one solo since this one actually sees the table with another player.  With all of the expansions the variability and options are fantastic.  The game is very thematic and a story really plays out in front of you.  Looking forward to even more plays of this one in the future.

RATING: 8
Much to my surprise, I think this made Pandemic obsolete for me. It has obvious similarities (both are cooperative games where players choose a role then spend action points each turn, something bad happens at the end of each turn). 

Each has some randomness (dice in Flash Point, card distribution in Pandemic). A big difference (apart from theme) is that in Pandemic, players are trying to collect and trade sets of cards while in Flash Point players are trying to rescue victims. I find the latter much more straight-forward and fun.

I'm surprised that I like this one so much, but I logged 13 plays in the first week I owned it. The variety in maps is just extra goodness.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
Naturally Flash Point compares closely to Pandemic, which is one my favorite cooperative games.  I like that Flash Point supports up to 6 players, allows action points to be carried over to future turns, and provides quite a variety of roles.

Where Pandemic outshines Flash Point is the manner in which the crisis grows.  In Pandemic, the reshuffling of the infection discards creates a somewhat predictable pattern to where the epidemics are most likely to occur.  This gives players the opportunity to strategize and plan how best to attack the most volatile areas.

In Flash Point, the roll of the dice basically means any point on the board is equally likely to be targeted.  Your team can still focus on rescuing victims and extinguishing fires, but your order of approach is more of a guess than based on how you think the fires will spread.  Winning and losing may be more a function of the dice rolls than anything else.  But playing Flash Point is still a fun activity.

RATING: 8
Ccop game with a relatively unique theme. I have played a lot games (1000s) and quite a few cooperative games (e.g., Shadows Over Camelot, Pandemic, Forbidden Island, Lord of the Rings, Castle Panic, Defenders of the Realm, Panic Station, etc.) and this is the best of 2011 and most likely in the Top 10 of cooperative games all time.  You are a firefighter.  Come on, who has not dreamed of being a firefighter?  Better yet, there is minimal chance of getting burned (unless you smoke or take the game to a different realism level) while you play.  Who could ask for more?  Game play is relatively simple and the spread of the fire is a great tension mechanism.  You have a several tactical choices (e.g., chop walls, move toward victims, etc.) and strategic decisions (e.g., fight fires or rescue victims).  In the advanced game (don't be scared by the word advanced, as it is still a relatively easy and straightforward game), your firefighters have special abilities and force you to work more cohesively as a team.  All in all, if you like the theme, or coops, or just want some new and different--then you should try Flash Point.  

Game Owned: #1730.  Game Played: #13140.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
[i]Flash Point[/i] reminds me just a little of [i]Pandemic[/i] in that its a coop-action board-management game, but its emphasis on getting people out rather then concentrating on the fire makes it much more focused and exciting, with a little extra randomness really heating things up.

Advanced mode is the way to go, and I think if you are playing the 'family'/basic mode you're basically only playing half a game.

It's quick (usually about 45 minutes to an hour per session) and although it's core rules system is quite light there's lots of depth to the game play. Although the base game only includes two static boards every game is very different.

The way fire acts, the way you can switch character roles as the situation changes (and in fact most of the elements of the game) are very well realised, and the game just feels very dynamic and intuitive. The major thing to take from this is its really fun!

Its very satisfying to play, feeling light and breezy whilst also being tactical and strategic.

Probably the only gripe I have is that some roles are not as effective as others meaning they tend to not get taken very often. Perhaps expansion boards will help these less essential roles find their place. Also there's no action tokens for the various roles despite several having specialised actions. This was fixed in the 2nd Story expansion but why they didn't have them in to start with is a mystery.

Talking of which the game is also well supported with several expansions adding all the depth and variation you could want onto to an already well greased and efficient system. Extra boards and more complicated rules add multiple floors to buildings, and introduce fire fighting in a warehouse, office block, subway station, aeroplane, and even ship and submarine!

More plays still might change my opinion yet but at this point its well on its way to becoming one of my all time favourite coops!

RATING: 3
I've wanted to like it so much and I've given it many chances, but FPFR just fails to capture how fun it sounds. The random fire rolls should prevent the alpha gamer planification issue common to most cooperative games - and perhaps they do to some extent - but unfortunately that effort is countered by most of the characters being dull and obvious. The extremely useful character powers generally make you focus exclusively on them, either because they're so powerful it would be waste to do anything else (right Mr. Truckdriver) or because they come bundled with an extremely limiting downside (your medic will almost never put out any fire). Then it's just an exercise in spending action points efficiently. I suspect the game is about character swapping rather than interesting characters, but at 4+ players you have all your angles covered and have no need to change them. (Aside from one player who just sits in a vehicle all day long, switching between the "scan POI" one and the "move other characters" one.) You will likely destroy the first levels of difficulty and harder ones just scale the fire up but don't force you to revise your strategy.

So I started buying expansions because trickier situations and variants would spice up the thing for sure, but they were in the vein of "how about victims that are conscious or heavy", "how about the fire truck accessing higher places", "how about the floor starting collapsing", "how about chemicals/submarine/airport/extinguishers/jammed-doors" and actually reveal the game's true nature as a top-down design that asks us to houserule it: since rules come down from what makes thematical sense, you might be blinded by all the chrome and overlook for a while that in the end, FPFR's mechanisms don't really escape their Pandemic heritage. Except the game is more fiddly than Pandemic, is more random than Pandemic, has more downtime than Pandemic, has more rules than Pandemic, has more unclear rules questions than Pandemic, has a longer setup time than Pandemic, is more prone to action points accounting than Pandemic and has less interesting decisions than Pandemic.

When the most fun part of your game is rolling the fire dice in the hope you'll have to deviate from the current perfect plan, you know there's something wrong. Also so many attempts at thematic integration to have your core mechanic be "fire and victims spawning at random places" feels like a waste.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-

RATING: 7
Nice little coop game, much in the same vein as Forbidden Island only without the cool artwork.  Good components though, and solid gameplay, a quality family game.


UPDATE:

Not played this in a while so we broke it out and actually convinced my staunchly non-gamer sister who was staying with us to join in.  The rules are simple and fast playing – although we opted for the basic game so as not to overwhelm my sister’s non-gamer brain - and it didn’t take much time to pick back up at all.  The family friendly coop theme makes me think of Forbidden Island, as does the simplicity, though FI has seen more play time.  We set up in 5 minutes flat, scanned the rules, and quickly managed to rescue a few peeps with my sister carrying all the animals out of the building, and me mostly catching false alarms, much to the others’ mirth (I make for a very lazy fireman apparently, who spends most of his time outside the building smoking fags).  Then the fires started breaking out in force and smashing the building up at the same time.  Before long we suffered two casualties to the smoke and flames, but we had rescued the requisite 7 victims to win the game.  Undeterred about the game actually ending we carried on to rescue the final victim just to see if we could.  And we did.  All in it took less than 30 mins and was good, family friendly fun.  My sister tried to hide the fact that she enjoyed herself enormously and then let us get back into the nerdier games where we get to blast things and slay monsters.  Great components, and clear gameplay.  Makes me wonder what Indie would have done with Fantasy Quest.

UPDATE 20/12/16 - I rate this alongside Forbidden Island and Desert as a solid, thematic family game, but with very little appeal for solo play.  Still, its appearance here reminds me I should buy some expansions as stocking fillers for the little one for Christmas...

RATING: 7
I gave this game another go recently, and I have to say it's a bit better than I remember. I actually like this game.

I don't really like playing with only one character each. I really feel like even if you're only playing with one other person, it's worth it to be playing with two people each. It makes the game a bit more interesting and keeps the house from burning down because firefighters are in multiple areas of the house.

It's a somewhat quick setup, and quick put away time. It's easy to teach, not too complicated to learn, and offers enough tactical flexibility to remain a fun game to play every now and again.

I would by no means consider this a game I could play all the time, but I can say that it's worth having in a collection and playing with people that are somewhat competent.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.3
Flash Point is a great co-op that comes recommended.

My wife and I are big co-op fans, with our favorite easily being Eldritch Horror. But while still being a co-op, Flash Point scratches a very different itch.

The setup takes just a few minutes and it plays pretty quickly, about 45.

Thematically, it immerses you in a unique and strangely fun environment - putting out a house fire trying to keep people from roasting. I thought this worked well for myself. But it could also work for someone that is put off by the common stock of board games: monsters, lazers, and spaceships (if you are unfortunate enough to know such a person).

The game also feels like it would scale very nicely with players. Although while I have not tried it with 6 (the max), it feels like there might be too many cooks in the kitchen. 2 to 4 strikes me as a good range.

RATING: 10
This game is our go to game and has been for the past two months.  Fired it up every weekend since getting it, played it with about 15 new people and they all couldn't get enough of it.

Flash Point: Fire Rescue plays similarly to Pandemic but there is more consistency to the difficulty.  Where you can have a string of bad luck happen enough that you will get blown out the water like Pandemic this happens a lot less frequently.

This is good because it allows for a more consistent tension throughout the game.  Bad things happen and you have to mitigate them, where as in Pandemic when the game starts to amp up and get exciting, you lose shortly after.

The only negative to the game is the game board which I feel is a clear notch down from Ticket to Ride which has a much larger game board and it feels a lot sturdier than FP:FR.

RATING: 7
The graphic design is nice and very functional, and the components are high quality.

Family level is very basic, with very simple rules, and very easy to solve, but its rules are very streamlined, perfect for family play. The advanced game is for gamers, with special abilities and more rules. It will still feel simple (concerning rules, not difficulty to beat it) to most gamers.

It feels very easy, even on veteran level, once you control the initial fire. Still, the game is fun, it is like a puzzle that changes constantly and forces you to adapt to it. I have not tried Heroic level, but I guess it can be too much. Of course, I imagine you can always house rule the setup to make it more difficult, but at the end, the outcome might depend more on dice rolls than in skill.

It is very thematic, the mechanics fit well with the theme, and even if there are some minor concessions, you never cease to believe this game is about putting out fires.

The characters are not that balanced, but since it's cooperative and you're allowed to change, there's no problem with that.

The difference bewteen 2st and 2nd edition is the wooden pawns vs plastic firefighter figures and wooden vs plastic cubes. Also, components (rules, reference cards, card names) were in German/English in the 1st edition, and now they're only in English.

First impressions [url=http://boardgamegeek.com/geeklist/173073/item/3562495#item3562495]here[/url].

RATING: 7
A pretty basic cooperative game where every player is a fireman trying to get victims out of a burning house. The way fire spreads is mechanically and thematically solid. Big plus for having a good theme but suffers from the most basic coop game problem that without any hidden information it is essentially a multiplayer solitaire game. Easiest to play with less players/firemen as then you get more actions between same firemen and fire doesn't spread that much between turns.

RATING: 8.5
One of the better co-ops I've played. What's nice about Flash Point is that it feels totally moddable based on the difficulty level that you'd like. It's easy and quick to swap fire trucks/hot spots/hazmats in and out of a game on the fly, so it's easy to teach but scales up to a brutal challenge.

Another interesting thing about this one is that it works really, really well with young kids and non-gamers. Where concepts like trading in cards for treasures in Forbidden Island can be difficult for my oldest boy, Flash Point's rules are just logical: "Dad, I'd like to put out that fire there." "Ok, son, you've got four points so you can put out these two or just this one and then move." It's very easy to translate what someone wants to do into the confines of the action point system.

Finally, the theme is great for a non-linear co-op. You can feel the immediacy of the threat as the fire grows larger and larger. For being such a Euro-inspired game, it sure has a great narrative every time.

RATING: 6
[b]Flash Point: Fire Rescue[/b] was sold via auction 4/4/15 (with 2nd Story expansion). 

[COLOR=#FF0000]A year later... thoughts and rating (6):[/COLOR]

[i]Another COOP that started with a bang and then fizzled out. The other two plays came in May 2014 (one month after we got it)  and then just sat on the shelf. I finally decided to get rid of a few weeks ago to make some room on our game shelves.

Flash Point is a good family game, but co-ops continue to not get played in my house (well except for Forbidden Island).[/i]

[COLOR=#FF0000]Initial thoughts and rating (8):[/COLOR]

[i]First I need to say that I am not a huge fan of Coops, but I wanted to try to find one that was thematic and that I could enjoy playing with my family. Long story short, Flash Point fills that niche in our collection.

Highlights:
- Awesome theme that is well integrated into the game mechanics.
- Great family game and since it is a coop you can potentially play with younger kids.
- Great bits that enhance the game.
- You actually feel the tension ratchet up as a house fills with smoke and fire.
- The group of characters you can play are all interesting and affect the game in different ways. Sometimes it does make sense to change the character you are playing as.[/i]

RATING: 7
心得:
還可以
但是擲骰的太頻繁有點累
骰子帶來的隨機也讓每場難度不大相同
隨機性稍微大些
規則:
*在圖板上的門放置門板塊，根據難度使用起始爆炸跟危險標記各3/3,3/4,4/5個，丟黑骰根據規則放第一個熱點跟火並處理一次爆炸，第二次擲兩顆骰決定，第三次黑骰翻面擲紅骰決定，如果點有重複則重新骰，都放熱點跟處理一次爆炸，如果有第四次則擲兩骰，要放不重複點，丟骰放對應數量個危險標記，有火重骰，移除兩個受害者標記跟一個誤報標記，其他翻面洗勻，丟骰放三個，如果有火就重骰，第二以上難度在擲骰放三次熱點(不重複位置)，在家兩個如果只有三個消防員，4個以上加3，放6/12(最難難度)個剩餘的到一旁
*每個人拿一個玩家卡跟特殊腳色卡跟對應顏色米寶放在圖板建築外任意格，並選擇位置放一個工程車跟救護車，自選起始
*遊戲輪流進行，每個玩家進行三個階段後換人，直到勝利或失敗條件
1.有四個行動點來做行動，可選行動如下，沒花完的行動點可存拿行動點標記，最多存四點
>移動到相鄰格 沒火一點，有火兩點，帶人2點(可經過有煙但不能有火)，不能停在以火的地方，移動到的點如果有問號標記就免費翻面(誤報標記就移除)，如果帶人到建築外直接獲救，移動到獲救區
>開關門 一點
>熄滅 可在該格或對相鄰格，移除煙一點，翻面火標記一點，
>砍 放一個傷害標記在牆兩點，有兩個傷害的牆被打破可通過
>工程車 在上面一起移動兩點，只能停在對應顏色區域，4點人在車上可發射水柱，擲骰，如果位置不再紅色虛線內(且虛線內不能有消防員)，骰子翻到對面，該格跟相鄰四格火或煙都移除(過牆不算)
>救護車 不用在上面，移動兩點，只能停在對應顏色區域
>換特殊卡 必須在工程車上，花兩點換一個沒使用的特殊腳色卡
2.丟兩顆骰並放煙在該位置，兩個煙變成一火，煙相鄰火直接變火，放火則爆炸，結算完後場上所有跟火相鄰的煙翻面，有火的問號標記移除放在失分區(可翻面)，有消防員在火上則被擊倒，之後移除建築物外的火
>爆炸時 上下左右如果空著相鄰各放一個火標記，有門則移除，煙變火，有強放傷害標記，如果有火則朝該方向延伸到第一個沒有火的區域，空地或煙放火，牆放傷害標記，門移除
>擊倒 放置該消防員在最近的救護車上，如果帶著受害者則直接失去
*危險標記如果有火在上面會爆炸，危險標記跟受難者一樣可帶走，帶出建築物外則移除
*如果擲骰結果在熱點上，放完火後會再擲一次加新的，且該輪如果有觸發，在最後一個放的位置再放上一個熱點，如果危險標記爆炸也放一個熱點
3.如果場上問號標記少於三(正反面都計)，則丟骰加一個新的，如果該位置有火則根據表格放在相應位置，還是沒地方放重骰
*遊戲在24個傷害標記用完結束，所有剩下的問號放到失去區，此時獲救區有7個人則獲勝，如果失去超過4個就失敗

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
A Pandemic style co-op, in that you get 4 action points to move around the board and/or eliminate fire (aka disease cubes) before the fire over-runs you and kills the victims lying there in the building before you rescue them. Again similarly, each player gets a special power that allows you to specialise (extra movement for rescuing victims, or extra actions for fighting fires, etc). Flash Point adds a load of randomness over Pandemic though in the construction and spread of the fire, all controlled by dice each turn. The explosion rules invoking a sudden spread of fire are a nice touch, adding drama to the game. And that's the game's great attribute (esp. over Pandemic) - the theme. You can put yourself in the building, rescuing victims, or wading around the edge of the fire pushing it back. It's also a theme that kids love, and this is easily playable by kids 8 and up. As a team you can choose to get the fire under control first and then start rescuing victims (which makes for a longer game) or just race to collect the victims and get them out of the building, fighting fires opportunistically. Allowing players to change roles mid-game provides for an interesting decision, but other than that the game is pretty straightforward. Turns are fast because the decisions aren't that hard once your strategy is decided - it's move or fight fire. It's probably a tad longer than Pandemic. This is for co-op fans who get fired up by the thematic appeal.

RATING: 8
What I like:
- VERY thematic, and the theme has wide appeal
- Simple to teach (especially the basic version)
- Interesting and deep (especially the advanced version)
- Plays quickly (45 minutes even with a few first-timers)
- Can work solo with a single firefighter
- Banking actions is genius, and switching roles mid-game is cool

What I don't like:
- With 6p, even though it's short, it can feel a bit long

I think the weight of 2.3 is about right, but a bit high if anything. It is comparable to Pandemic in complexity and replayability. FP:FR might be slightly more random/swingy thanks to the dice.

This was a 9 for me for a long time, but recently I just found myself less interested in playing it. Even more recently, I lost a family member in a house fire, so I doubt I'll play again for a bit. Not the game's fault, of course, and even before that tragedy, it really was an 8.

DISCLAIMER: [b]I was a playtester for FP:FR[/b]. I bought the earlier Flash Point predecessor on my own, and had posted nice things about it on BGG. Then I was asked to be a playtester for FP:FR, and happily did so. When the kickstarter project came along, I signed up so I could get a copy with the improved rules and components.

RATING: 7
I'm not a huge fan of cooperative games, but this is one of the better ones out there.  Each player takes on a role, which will help them either put out the fire or save victims.  You can actually change roles mid-game, though generally this is more effort than it's worth.  So you run around, discovering if certain spots contain real victims or are just red herrings, and try to get them out before the house burns down.  Each player's turn is, of course, followed by the spreading of fire.  If you rescue a certain number of victims, then you win.  The game is very thematic, and the cooperative nature fits right into the theme.

RATING: 6
Solid fun co-op. Enjoyable theme for everyone I think. Easier for groups to get into.

Plays fast. We can finish a game in under 45 min. 

A little over rated. More tactical and reactionary than other games of its type. Family game is for kids. The advanced game is the proper way to play.

The expansions are nice challenging additions to add some variety and breath new life into the game. Recommended if you like the game.

edit: Despite improving greatly at this game there is only so much you can do to influence a win. 2 wins 7 loses is painful. 

I like a hard game, but this is hard in a way that's largely outside your control. The randomness is just too chaotic. Poor play rewards you with a 100% loss rate. Exceptional play rewards you with a 30% success rate depending on map, your team, and conditions. 

The Fire captain, Deck-gun operator, and Generalist are critical to success and should always be on the team. loses are usually due to building collapse. This is why they added a structural engineer to the expansion to help with that.
The more people that play the harder the game gets.

It's a fun group co-op experience, but the lack of control and success, is hurting the game for us. Probably keep it around for the non-gamers.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9
Really good coop game about rescuing people out of a burning building before it collapses.

A few fires are out at the start of the game and then smoke spreads each player turn. All smoke adjacent to fire also becomes fire, so at times a buildup in a closed room can be a real nailbiter. All it takes is a single spark and there is fire everywhere. At that point the walls can collapse really fast.

The game has different roles with the possibility of spending actions to switch roles to gain the capabilities of different specialists.

Three levels of difficulty and a two sided board with an easy and a difficult side make for a varied experience.

One important difference when compared to my other favorite coops, Pandemic and Eldritch Horror, is that this game does not have a timer. The two other games have the Player deck and Mythos deck respectively that are drawn from every turn and if you must draw a card but can't, you've lost. The lack of timer allows for a slower, more methodical approach to playing. As long as the fire is under control you're good.

This game scratches the same itch as Pandemic but different enough that I probably would add it to my 40+ game collection if I couldn't play someone elses copy.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
10+ (8+) Best 4 (Rec 1-3) 45mins

Another co-operative design which easily allows players jump in or out of a session, making it a great "entry" game if someone is hovering about interested in what is going on. (In Flash Point it adds to the theme: "hooray, another unit has arrived/oh no, call an ambulance").

Because of the miniatures, the board, the fire tokens, the actions of chopping etc and the way the fire behaves makes it easier to translate into an exciting drama, making it marginally better than the cube spreading diseases of Pandemic. 

Yes the die-rolling in Flash Point adds a lot of randomness compared to the draw deck of Pandemic, but I feel because of the unpredictable (and thematic) way the threat is done means less firm data for the alpha attitude (it happens) to stamp control on other players decisions and moves.

My only quibble is it seems the family rules and set up make the game too easy, but maybe it is the "front side" of the board that makes it less challenging. For me it is easier to explain during advance randomising set up what explosions do (especially using the marker from 2nd story) and shockwaves, adding hot spots and damage markers where applicable. This seems to make the game more dramatic and quicker game end. Adding these rules and the advance placement rule of POI reduces the vibe of too much die rolling and making placement quicker.

A great theme for a co-op. While I enjoyed the game, resolving explosions/shockwaves felt more fiddly than I would have liked, and I still don't quite understand how the deck gun works. RATING: 7.5
Pros:
* Co-op. If you don't think that's a pro, there's not much point in looking any further at this game.
* Once you get the hang of it, the turns are really quick.
* The "Rising Water" mechanic feels nicely thematic. A collapsed building is a more dramatic ending than running out of a draw deck. It's also kind of neat that there's some benefit (shortcuts) to having the walls blow up.

Neutral:
* Suffers from typical co-op issues - it's just a puzzle you're solving together, an alpha player can ruin it for everyone, the game gets easier as you both get better at it rather than becoming more challenging as your (human) opponent improves, etc.

Comparisons:

* While I can't say if I like it better than Pandemic, it does have a similar feel. I never liked the hand-management part of Pandemic that requires you to stategize around swapping cards back and forth (especially when you play by the rules instead of keeping them face up on the table). FP doesn't have that issue.

= 2014-08-08 - R:7.5

I don't actually know if I like Flash Point (FP) more than Pandemic (P). It's been a long time since we played P and our tastes have changed a bit over time. I also don't know if FP feels all that different from P. In both cases, we've only ever played with the base game (no expansions) and in the case of FP, we haven't even played with the full rules yet (still no hazmats, still counting people save as soon as they get outside, still having new POIs clear the smoke/fire of the location they land on).

Both that's not the point. The game is fun and good co-ops are rare enough to justify both just so you can keep things fresh. Which brings us to co-ops in general. I visited my brother a couple months ago and we played Zombicide. One of the reasons I have such a hard time getting through my collection of games is I dread teaching people the rules for a game. If it's a game I already know how to play, I know it's going to take a couple plays before the new player is competitive (one of the reasons we like games with high luck). Co-ops go a long way towards "solving" both of those "problems". I sat down to play Zombicide, they handed me a character and let me be the 4th of 4 players on the first round. That was pretty much the extent of our pre-game tutorial. Because it's a co-op, people are (more than) willing to help you play and teach you as you go along. You could go to the bathroom and let someone play your character without having to worry that he'll purposefully play suboptimally. A couple weeks ago, we sat down with a non-gamer and taught him how to play FP in much the same way; here's your character, here's what you can chose to do. Watch us do our turns first and then we'll tell you what your options are on your turn. Go!

I have a new love for co-ops and FP gets a good bit of the credit for that.

RATING: 7.5
I really enjoy this game. This is one of my favorite Co-ops. It offers a family mode that is great for the family and an advanced mode that offers substantial decision making and challenges. The game moves fast and does not overstay its welcome. The theme of rescuing people from burning houses, and the d8/d6 grid to roll for fire spread creates a real feeling of suspense as you try and rescue the 7 victims. I usually would not like the dice rolls and all the luck for co-ops, but it makes since in this game because I'm sure fire is unpredictable as well. Overall, a very solid co-op game with a great difficulty range. The mechanics really fit the theme, and it doesn't always slaughter you like many co-ops. **Wife:8

RATING: 9.88
Flash Point: Fire Rescue is a really good co-operative game.  In fact, I think it might be my current favorite co-operative game.  I like the banked actions to save for later when you feel like you would be wasting them, and the chaotic dice rolls for spreading the fire make it feel a little more exciting to me than Pandemic (which is probably now my 2nd favorite co-operative game).  Flash Point is more straight forward than Ghost Stories, and to me actually feels a little more of a gamer's game than Pandemic due to the switching of roles at critical times and the varied tasks that need done to save people and pets from a burning building/structure.  A great game!

RATING: 7
Component Quality:
Outstanding. Among the best i've seen from a game. Especially surprised by the kickstarter Firemeeples.

Gameplay:
The game flows very smoothly. Each role is fairly specialized so there's not a lot of downtime deciding actions. The spreading of the fire is actually pretty ingenious and makes for a chaotic good time. A TON of extra options for game setup, especially with the Urban Structures expansion, meaning it's very hard for the game to ever grow stale. Definitely one of my favorite cooperative games.

RATING: 8
Very similar to Pandemic, but currently I enjoy it a bit more, especially for solo play (it is easier to manage multiple firemen, since they don't have hands of cards).  Quicker setup and even though there are dice, it feels a little less random.  The visuals of a house with fire tokens and broken walls feels more immersive than the piles of cubes across a map.  Turns go by really fast and there's more potential for team work, like one person putting out fires so another player has a safe route back to carry their victim.  The only drawback I see right now is that there is no doomsday clock on the game like running out of cards in Pandemic.  Since you control the pace that the victims come into play, as long as the victims aren't in imminent danger, you can always basically stop rescuing and just focus on putting out all the fires with no penalty.  It is also strange thematically that new victims keep appearing just at the moment that you rescue one - I keep imagining my firearm saying "Damn little dog - were you hiding in the toilet? I've already been in this bathroom 3 times!" I might try a variant where a new victim appears every X turns (in addition to adding them when you go below 3 on the board).

Flash point is a really popular game where players play as firefighters working together to put out fires breaking out in a home. Cons: Rules are a little disjointed in my opinion. movement efficiency game play focus. No real variety it appears in gameplay. For the them there is a lack of tension.

RATING: N/A
Play as firefighters in a burning building. The objective of the game is to control the fire while trying to rescue people and take them to safety. Each player can take a certain number of moves and actions per turn, but after each turn the fire spreads. Rolling the dice decides where the fire goes and might cause an explosion making the fire spread even faster. Players work together as a team and can take on specialized roles, each with unique capabilities. One player might specialize in rescuing victims, increasing their movement ability. Another might specialize in putting out fires, where they can't move quite as far but are able to put out more fire. 

Every roll for the placement of the fire is tense and watching it spread can feel overwhelming, yet exciting. It is like a puzzle that is constantly shifting. Players have to adapt their strategy to new conditions.  

The game can be difficult and sometimes your team looses. Loosing in this game feels a bit different than they typical competitive game. One person doesn't win and another loose, so it doesn't create animosity or envy like some games might. Instead you win or loose as a team. Loosing makes it feel like a challenge that you want to overcome, learn from the previous game, and try again.

RATING: 6
Good light conversational family game - tested on kids as young as six and they get the strategy well. Can't imagine suggesting it to adults though. As a cooperative game the wife won't touch it, but it's so easy and thematic the kids can set it up, explain and play it with their friends.

A simple enough system to pick up - move your fire people around using an action point system, putting out fires and rescuing people and pets. The base game is good for learning the system and then add all the bells and whistles from the experienced game as soon as you can.

There are a decent number of decisions to be made - more so in the experienced game - that it's not completely obvious what the best move is (but not altogether far from being obvious either). Players feel more independent than in other cooperative games I've tried, like Pandemic and Forbidden Island, where here you're not handing cards over to other players, but rather spread out when needed and directing points of urgency between each other. As a result turns are faster because there's less need for coordination, and the game has far less chance of being dominated by one player - which is good when a group of kids are playing by themselves.

Essentially the game is made by the cool theme. Who doesn't want to save people from a burning building from the safety of your dining room table? A game I'm happy to join in with the kids for some family time.

RATING: 7.2
A thematic, tense co-operative game of fighting fires and saving people from danger which uses an action point allowance system as it's central mechanism.

Players use their allotted action points to run around a house-floor-plan game board, extinguish flames and smoke, chop through walls, drag victims to safety, and even fire the deck gun on the firetruck.

After using her/his points (or saving them for the next turn), each player will roll two dice and consult the numbered grid around the edge of the board to see where the fire spreads. Too much fire can cause victims to be lost and the house to become damaged and eventually collapse.

I like this game very much, but am having trouble finding a good balance of rules and difficulty for my play group. At first, we won every time. Then, I added more hotspots and hazardous materials and we have lost several times in a row... I'm considering adding the option of playing as the Structual Engineer (expansion role) who can prop up the building to delay its collapse (building collapse is the #1 way to lose in Flash Point). I'll print the rules off of the "Urban Structures" page and give it go.

Overall, a fun game system that is fairly accessible to new players and which is not overly-prone to an "alpha gamer" telling everyone what to do.

RATING: 8
Excellent game!

One of the better co-op games that works well for solo players.
The Theme is well integrated with the mechanics and the component quality and artwork also help build atmosphere.
The base game has a heap of replay ability but when you start adding expansions it goes through the roof. I still haven't explored all the options available.
Each character requires minimal bookkeeping so it is easy to play multi-handed, but the game also scales well, meaning playing with two characters is both fun and effortless.

I think this game will always stay in my Top 10. :)

I go back and forth over whether I enjoy this one more than Pandemic. I feel like the roles really focus your strategy in this game more so than Pandemic. I also like the randomness of the dice more than the card deck. There's just something about throwing those dice, hoping for anything but one result. This game captures the feeling of rescuing people from a burning building quite well. I always save the pets first, of course.

RATING: 8
This is the best light/mid weight cooperative game that we have played. Pandemic/Forbidden Island/Forbidden Desert all have the same puzzle of card drawing in locations that have already been hit, and that is fine, but it means that an experienced player is either going to quarterback the game, or watch in horror as the companions make a series of non-optimal moves. Not so in Flash Point. The dice rolling mechanic for spreading fire is a perfect way of making sure no ones knows exactly what is going to happen and thus be able to "solve" the puzzle. It has a fun theme and the variety of fire fighter roles makes it fun and changes each game up from the last.

RATING: 7.75
A very simple (with the Family Rules) co-operative game that is still fun and tense.  The simplicity of the turn sequence lets you concentrate on the game play and strategy, but the fire is relentless, especially when there are explosions and Shockwaves going on.  Cheer when you save a victim or a pet, and be sad when a victim (or pet) is engulfed or your Fireman is knocked down (and sent to the Ambulance) by the expanding fire.  Brilliantly done, very nicely produced, and easy to follow rules.  With plenty of expansions and accessories adding variety and greater difficulty.  Highly recommended.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 9.3
I like this co-op game and the theme. It is probably my most played co-op.

There are a lot of little things to keep up with during the game, which is a challenge at first but not so much after playing a few games. For example: rules for advancing the fire, placing new hot spots (Flare Ups and Hazmat explosions), rules for replenishing POI's, the special abilities and restrictions on various Specialists, and what to do at each step in a turn.  I had to add AP counters/markers to keep track on how many actions I spent, and I also got a 'current player' marker to keep that detail straight too (a Matchbox fire engine, lol).

Solo
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
I just sat down and played a "family" game.  I played solo with four firefighters, and lost the first game--I let one room get out-of-control such that there were multiple explosions in it that eventually caused enough damage the house collapsed on my guys and the un-rescued folks within. You have to save at least 7, and as they start out as unknowns, something like five of the markers I "rescued" were actually "false alarms"--no one there--and only four actual people rescued (and unlike in the shows, the dog died along with the firefighters and other occupants).

I played at the "family" level which is six pages of rules.  I read the rules last night and knew I had to get it to the table ASAP--it looked really slick.  After one play the "family" level might be a tad more complicated than Ticket to Ride, but not by much.  The Advanced rules add another four pages and several features, including specialist "roles" for your firefighters (in the family mode they all play the same).  The expansion board (see below) rules, about high-rises/brownstones, add yet more rules, although I think they could be tacked on to either the family or advanced rules sets.

The rules were pretty good, although there are a few weaknesses in the explanations of explosions and, especially, shockwaves--I need to look on the 'geek for clarification there.  Other than that, though, it was a lot of fun in my first go.  I think I'll try a few more times at family level before going on to the advanced game.  After that, I'd feel confident enough to teach it to others.  It would make a *great* iPad game (hint, hint ;)

This was my very first Kickstarter project/product.  I paid enough that I got the "Urban Structures" expansion (with a new double-sided board (brownstone and high-rise), rules, and a new specialist card) and a set of wooden fireman/woman meeples--way cool!

After one play, recommended, but we'll see what legs it has.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This is a Pandemic-style co-op game where the tragedies occur on a more local, less global, scale.  Which brings me straight into one of the things I don't like about the game: the fact that you can lose a couple of victims to the flames and still win the game!  (As a paramedic, that doesn't quite sit right with me.)  And while we're being negative (don't tell Travis!), the "Advance Fire" phase is overly fiddly and confusing, and the dice-based system leads to more randomness than the card system in Pandemic (that crazy ol' fire just keeps popping up all over the place!).  Oh, it's also illustrated by George Patsouras, creator of lifeless, doll-like board game characters that inexplicably make me want to vomit.  But now that all that is out of my system, I will say that the game is an enjoyable and tense co-operative experience.  And the production values of the most recent edition of the game, particularly with the individually sculpted firefighter minis, are simply outstanding!  The difficulty level is very scaleable, and the replayability is high, between the number of firefighter characters that can be chosen, the double-sided game board, and the randomness of the appearance of the fire.  Game design: 3.5/5  Personal enjoyment: 3.5/5  Total: 7/10
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
Co-op game about firefighters rescuing people from a burning building. Fire spreads extremely unpredictably (based on a die rolls), and often explosively; the full game includes rules for explosive hazardous materials, a fire truck throwing on water from outside, and the steady rise in heat that can accelerate the blaze.

The randomness seems much less controllable than Pandemic, as well as annoyingly fiddly. The effect of rolling to advance the fire ranges from placing a harmless smoke token to causing an explosion that creates 4 more fires (i.e. more than 8x variance in impact with no possibility of mitigation). Placing victims is also done at random, perhaps at the feet of a firefighter or perhaps in the middle of a blazing room -- though in this case I actually mind the randomness less than the unthematic absurdity of four of them appearing at different times in the same bathroom, as though the firefighters tromping through mistook successively mistook them for heaped towels.

Pressure builds nicely, characters are varied, and there is evidently room to shake things up (see also: numerous expansions). While I think strictly worse than Pandemic as a system, for mechanical reasons, the wide variety on offer would make it a winner if played often.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7
This is an interesting one. It's a fun co-op game but it suffers feels more like a group of people playing a single-player game than most co-op games I've played. It feels like there are always one or two really good ideas and everything is either utterly out of control or perfectly manageable. At times it commits one of the bigger sins of co-op gaming: being too easy.

That said, it's fun when things are properly crazy and the fire mechanics make the designer in me really, really happy. The game works as I think it's intended, too. I think it's trying to be a lighter, less punishing co-operative game with enough flexibility to crank up the difficulty to taste. I would highly recommend this game as a solo experience, but as a cooperative one ... I wouldn't turn down a play, but I wouldn't recommend it over Pandemic or Ghost Stories either. 

It doesn't feel like enough of a brain-bender; Pandemic has a bit of this problem as well and it's why I prefer Ghost Stories. At their most difficult, the former two games make me feel like the inevitable occurred and we were doomed. We just couldn't have done anything. In Ghost Stories, those plays certainly happen ... but they aren't as characteristic of a brutal session in my experience. Typically it feels like we could have done something else. The very simplicity of Pandemic and Flash Point makes them feel like less of a puzzle. It might be that the puzzle-like feeling of Ghost Stories is illusory, but I always feel like I could have optimized my use of the many subsystems better. All three games are about mitigating risk rather than solving an exact puzzle but I feel like Ghost Stories gives you both more risk and more tools with which to mitigate it making for a game that is more difficult to learn, far more difficult to win, and at the same time more fair. To anyone who finds Ghost Stories (or for that matter Pandemic) too difficult and opaque, Flash Point can get you your co-operative fix in a more accessible package. The theme is exquisitely rendered and there's immense potential for creating more challenging scenarios and set-ups even without opting for the several expansions already on their way.

RATING: 8.5
One of my favorite game. You can easily adjust the difficulty of the game if you find it too easy.

The game is also really modular. You can play with roles or vanilla firefighters, with amublance and firetruck or not, with hotspots or not, with hazardous material or not...

Lots of flexibility.

The game requires a lot of teamwork. You have to balance managing the fire and rescuing victims. Some appear in spots that are difficult to reach: Do you break through the wall, and run the risk of the building coming down on your head, or take the long way around, at the risk of seeing the victim die in a fire?

It did happen a few times that the game was lacking in tension, but most of the time it is great fun. 

The actions you do on your turn are not that exciting taken in isolation (move 2 spaces and remove one fire marker), but fighting the fire as a team is rewarding and fun.

Tried two expansions: second story and urban structure. They are ok, but I find the base game much more fun.

RATING: N/A
#Players: 1-6

Pull people from a burning building as a fire rescue team. Choose a specialty and assist the team in rescuing as many people as possible before the building collapses.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
One of the most enjoyable games I know that can be played in less than an hour, Flash Point Fire Rescue is a superior, more detailed variation of a dire situation game like Pandemic. Instead of dealing with abstractions in a distant global setting, FPFR puts the players (or player) in a burning house where collapsing walls, exploding hazmats, and imperiled victims compete for every precious action point while the second hand of destruction moves forward.
A good combination of luck and skill, this game is a fun and exciting losing battle in which players must make life saving and life ending decisions every turn and hope that the courses chosen and the courses neglected result in the most saved people.
The character skills also mix things up nicely, though maybe the Imaging Technician's special skill of identifying Points of Interest is too powerful (choosing that character really improved my success rate right away), but the game is smart, exciting, and the deployment of the vehicles is an especially fun variable. Behold the deck guns!
Unlike Agricola (which is clever but has far too much piece relocation/counting for my taste), Pandemic (which is fairly decent but kind of annoying and very abstract), and Catan (which I thought was quite dull), Flash Point Fire Rescue is a good gateway game that fires my gamer imagination and can show off the merits of modern board games to curious non-gamers as well. A simple but instantly engrossing struggle against ever worsening odds with depth and a bunch of nice details.

RATING: 3
A cooperative game with a strong theme.

I have a soft spot for cooperative games with a universally accepted theme. This game is spot on in this matter. It's a great introductory cooperative game and it's quite easy and fun to play. The various roles and the random set up make it replayable enough but...

...the mechanics don't really keep up. Although the game is fun and flows relativily well, there is little room for cooperation or choices. There is a bit of downtime as well. It's more of a decent movie that unfolds while the players make the obvious choices just to keep their interest fixed.

I can tolerate this game with new players and I'll accept to play it either as a gateway game or as a relaxing pass-the-time game. There are much better co-op games although few better themed than this one.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 6
A cooperative game of fire rescue.

The call comes in... "911, what is your emergency?" On the other end is a panicked response of "FIRE!" Moments later you don the protective suits that will keep you alive, gather your equipment and rush to the scene of a blazing inferno. The team has only seconds to assess the situation and devise a plan of attack - then you spring into action like the trained professionals that you are. You must face your fears, never give up, and above all else work as a team because the fire is raging, the building is threatening to collapse and lives are in danger.

You must succeed. You are the brave men and women of fire rescue, people are depending on you. This is what you do every day.

Flash Point: Fire Rescue is a cooperative game. All the players are on the same team and everyone either wins or loses together. To win, the players must rescue the victims trapped inside a burning building before the fire gets out of control or the building collapses.

RATING: 7
Only played the family game sofar, but it was pretty good fun. The game is easy to grasp and plays quickly with little downtime. The theme fits the gameplay perfectly. That said, the randomness of allocating smoke counters (by making numerous dice rolls) makes it hard to anticipate potential risk areas like in, for example, Pandemic. I feel more "in control" in Pandemic, which automatically leads to a greater sense of urgency in the second half of the game. So as long as I own Pandemic, I feel no need to own this game as well (even though I would gladly try the advanced version next time).
UPDATE: Tried the advanced version, and think it is much more interesting to play than the family game. The different roles are all useful, and it is really neat that you can change yours in the middle of a turn!

RATING: 7
This game gets criticized a lot for being more random compared to games like Pandemic.  But such critics are missing the point.  The randomness allows everyone to participate because the bossy player syndrome is less prevalent here.  Players do their assigned jobs and deal with the crisis as it evolves.  Because it's not possible to really predict what will happen the better players can't hijack the game.

Pandemic might be deeper, but I'll bet this game ends up being played more by more people.  The problem of the bossy player in co-ops is fairly significant.  Flash Point is a great co-op that allows everyone to have fun.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 2
I must say, I'm extremely disappointed with FP:FR so far. Player turns are so exceedingly obvious, they practically play themselves. If I'm near a victim, get them and carry them out. If I'm near fire, extinguish it. Otherwise, move to fire or a victim. That's because ultimately, there's only two things you do, move or put out fire. You look at the reference card and think there's lot of different things, but ultimately they all come back to these two. Move. Move through fire. Move with victim. Chop wall (so you can move through it). Move the ambulance. Move the truck.

Everything that's great about Pandemic is missing here. In three games, there hasn't been a single moment of real discussion about options "Carry that guy out? Yup." "Put out that fire? Yup." Pandemic has so many moments of planning, should we meet up here, or build that research station, or treat disease, or play our special cards? The order you do things can have massive differences in results, and there's always great discussion. Here? None of it.

Also missing is the future planning. In Pandemic, it's very common to come up with moves multiple turns ahead, with the various players all working together and using their roles to facilitate the planning. "Ok, Bob goes to Paris, and builds a research station. Then, Nancy will be able to move Bill to that station on her turn. Bill now can get the Paris card from Harriet, and cure the final disease to win, just fractions of a second before we lose!"

FP:FP just doesn't have this. It's due to the totally random nature of fire and victims. You roll the dice at turn end, and add smoke/fire and victims to the locations shown. The end result is anything can happen on a turn. You're standing in a room, and fwap, suddenly a new victim is right beside you making for an easy rescue. Or, it appears in an area flush with fire, virtually guaranteeing they'll be toast soon. There might be a large danger area of fire, but the new fire appears in an empty closet miles away from anything and you have lots of time to get it under control. Or, there might be a victim in a completely fire free area, leading you to believe that you have time to fight fire elsewhere, then suddenly one turn smoke appears, then next turn it explodes into 5 fires killing them.

The brilliance of the Pandemic deck mechanism is that it's variable, but it's not random. As the game progresses, you learn where the hotspots are developing and you *know* something will strike there. The card deck content is fixed, but in variable order.

It might be thematic that fire is totally random, but it's not very interesting.

edit: Sold.

RATING: 8
------------------------------
NOTICE : Due to my poor spoken & written English, the rest of my comments will be written in French only but you can read my profile for more informations about the kind of games I prefer and how I rated them.
------------------------------

►ÉDITION : Indie boards and cards, français, 2012.
Éditeur, nb joueurs : 1 à 6 joueurs.
Éditeur, durée : 0h45.
Éditeur, âge : 10 ans et plus.

►PUBLIC(S) QUE JE RECOMMANDE:

VERSION FAMILIALE:
☺ Jeu thématique (ex : coop ou semi-coop, améritrash, univers adapté).
☺ Jeu familial (pour jeunes et/ou adultes).
     
VERSION AVANCÉE:
☺ Jeu thématique (ex : coop ou semi-coop, améritrash, univers adapté).

►JOUEURS, NOMBRE(S) QUE JE RECOMMANDE:
# Meilleur :
# Recommandé : 2, 3, 4
# Non-recommandé :
# Non-essayé : 1, 5, 6
1 joueur : je n’ai pas d’intérêt pour les configurations en solo.

►COMMENTAIRE(S) ABRÉGÉ(S):
+ THÈME : assez présent; relativement bien intégré.
+ Aide de jeu : 1 par joueur. Bien détaillé.
+ Expériences multiples : version familiale et version avancée.
+ Expériences multiples : personnages individuels personnalisés.
+ Expériences multiples : plusieurs niveaux de difficulté.
+ Icônes : sont faciles à comprendre ou à mémoriser.
+ Règles : flexibles; les règles peuvent être adaptées aux joueurs (de facile à plus difficile).

►REMARQUE(S) PERSONNELLE(S):
Jeu où les joueurs incarnent une équipe de pompiers combattant un incendie dans le but de sauver des victimes d’un bâtiment en feu avant que celui-ci ne soit hors de contrôle ou que le bâtiment s’effondre.

Un des premiers jeux coopératifs que je montrerais à des joueurs n’ayant jamais essayé un jeu de ce genre pour les raisons suivantes :
1e- le thème fait appel à une réalité connue de tous.
2e- les règles et mécaniques sont assez bien reliées au thème, ce qui facilite leur assimilation.
3e- la propagation du feu étant aléatoire, l'action optimale à faire n'est jamais certaine ce qui a l’avantage de diminuer l’impact d’un potentiel "joueur-alpha" qui voudrait dicter les actions de chacun.
4e- la version « Familiale » permet d’éviter que des joueurs non-habitués à collaborer subissement une défaite accablante dès la 1e partie et que le découragement s’installe.

Autrement, pour les habitués de la coopération, la version « Avancée » ajoute des modules supplémentaires, modifie quelques-unes des règles de base et présente 3 niveaux de difficulté (recrue, vétéran, héroïque) ce qui renouvelle les défis à relever. À noter que certains commentaires reprochent au jeu que les cartes « Pompier-spécialiste » obligent les joueurs à jouer leurs actions selon leur spécialisation avec peu de possibilité d’en déroger. Habituellement, c’est un point qui m’irriterait aussi mais puisque les pompiers spécialisés existent réellement, je trouve que cet aspect du jeu se justifie ici.

►EXTENSION(S) ESSAYÉE(S):
& "Flash point : Fire rescue / Fire academy challenge" : Non (pas intéressée à jouer solo).
& "Flash point : Fire rescue / 2nd story" : À essayer.
& "Flash point : Fire rescue / Urban structures" : À essayer.

►JEU(X) COMPARABLE(S) ESSAYÉ(S) :
Bien que j’ai aussi joué à d’autres jeux coopératifs, aucun d’entre eux ne me semble assez comparable pour l’instant.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 5
Like most cooperative games, Flash Point creates tension by ramping up the challenge exponentially each turn and giving you limited actions to use to complete your conflicting objectives.  Your incentives change based on the state of the game, and the variety of the roles and the randomness of the placement of the hazards make the game different each time, even if you play on the same board.  And if this sounds a lot like Pandemic, then you can see where I'm going.  Pandemic created the formula for a successful cooperative game, and Flash Point does a good job of duplicating it with a different theme and a small tweaking to the mechanisms.  Theme-ing the game to be about rescuing individuals from a fire is a bit less abstracted than curing diseases on a global scale, so the game succeeds in making your actions feel more immediately satisfying, but the game still feels like a cooperative game, and I'm just not that fond of them.  I think folks who like cooperative games will like Flash Point just fine, but not me.

1 play: 2 players

RATING: 7
This is yet another iteration of the very successful Pandemic co-op engine. The most unique feature of this title is using dice to spread the fire, instead of cards. Dice are extremely unpredictable by their nature, resulting in a fire that is constantly jumping around and sometimes even doubling back on itself. This unpredictability fits the firefighting theme extremely well, leaving you nearly always in danger of losing control of the situation. The tension comes on quickly and usually sticks around, making almost every session an exciting endeavor.

The only disappointing thing about the game is its graphic design. The role cards look fantastic, but parts of the board and almost all of the tokens look like really bad clip art. I know they didn't necessarily want photo-realistic charred corpses for when things go bad, but the faceless paper doll looking things are just plain weird and sort of jarring.

On a related note, I'm seriously starting to consider putting Pandemic out to pasture. I've found that Defenders of the Realm provides so much more flexibility to the players, by not making them rely entirely on the draw deck to function. Flash Point: Fire Rescue on the other hand, offers a much more unpredictable "villain" that can attack anywhere at any time. This keeps the players on their toes and makes the game less of a solvable puzzle and more of a dynamic, tactical challenge. These two games both correct what I considered to be minor flaws with Pandemic, the min/maxed programmed relationships between the roles, the importance of turn order, and the obvious pattern of outbreaks all lead to a very predictable experience.

Having access to both of these second generation Pandemic-styled games, I find myself playing the original less and less. If this holds my interest as well as Defenders of the Realm has, I may have to pull the trigger on letting Pandemic go.

RATING: N/A
Co-op firefighting and rescue. Players have special roles. Random setup with dice coordinates for hot spots that catch fire, then place hazards and potential victims depending on difficulty level. 911 call is made to dispatch. Action point system to rescue the occupants and their pets or make sure they were just false alarms and save the house before it burns to the ground. You can save unspent action points for the following turn is different. Light, thematic, gateway into cooperative gaming.

RATING: 6.5
A better family coop than Pandemic, primarily because Flash Point is more concrete in its urgency and context.  A raging fire that spreads from room to room and puts people/pets in danger is more tangible than a disease that spreads from continent to continent and threatens to extinguish the entire human race.

That said, there's already a better Pandemic for families: Forbidden Island, which is a Gamewright reworking of the original Z-Man hit.  Both Forbidden Island and Flash Point are fairly random, so deciding between the two is probably a matter of thematic appeal.

RATING: 8
Invariable, this game will be compared to [thing=30549][/thing] and [thing=65244][/thing] because these games can be played with families and non-gamers. This is a different game than Pandemic, and in my mind the family game is easier to grasp for children compared to Pandemic. I have played Pandemic with my 10yo and she had trouble grasping that game. Sharing cards and making sets to cure diseases in the realm of Pandemic is fairly abstract. Fighting fires and rescuing people off the board is tangible.

Can this game be dictated by an overly strong player? Yes, this is an issue with all cooperative games and this is no different. However, during the game there are so many things that needed to be done it is hard to say what was the right choice. By adding some other items, specialist cards, hazardous materials (cause explosions), vehicles (victims must be taken to the ambulance, the firetruck can be used to quickly put out fire), fire intensity, the game can be quickly ratcheted up in complexity to cater to different levels of gamers.

In the end, the theme is a great one. Firefighters fighting fires, chopping walls to get to the noise they hear in the next room or to escape a wall of fire with the family dog, driving fire trucks, etc. is one that can appeal to a broad range of groups. My son summed up the theme best when asked what he liked about the game, "I liked the game because I could be a fireman and rescue people."

Includes [gameid=110139], [gameid=126954], [gameid=140552] and [gameid=139766]

RATING: 9
[b]Comments after my first 2 plays:[/b]
My rating is only based on having played the Family version of the game, and it is really good. We will definitely play this regularly.

This is a very fun coop, the dice rolling does of course increase the randomness somewhat, but it can be mitigated through good play, and that's part of the game's charm.

The theme shines through in a big way, and it's simply fun to play firefighters.

I also own the 2nd Story and Urban Structures expansions, and with all the double sided boards we should be able to explore this game for a very long time.

[b]Comments after 3 more plays with a gaming buddy and having tried the Experienced Game:[/b]
The game actually got a lot better, as suspected, with the Experienced Game. It really is a thrill to play. Sure, there's a lot of randomness with the dice rolling, but you can still mitigate that with good play. I also find that the Hot Spots and Hazmats lend a good sense of foreboding and allow you to focus your efforts in a good way, all to mitigate the luck factor.

Great game!

[b]Comments after 11 plays:[/b]
My opinion of the game was starting to dip until my 11th play, which redeemed it. The reason was that the randomness started really getting to me, especially as we were first playing with the Hot Spots, but again as you get used to them you see the thematic connection and how they are a sort of game timer in a sense, even if mostly a random one.

I also felt that saving action points and switching roles mid-game made it too easy. What cured me of these thoughts was playing regularly at the highest difficulty level. The game shines then, and basically has you arriving late to a house fire with little chance of saving everyone, except with highly tactical play.

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
It takes a while to set-up this game. Luckily for us, we always bag all of the components separately, which in the case of this game, that the insert of the box had to be adjusted to fit all of the components, but it would still give proper support to the board. After done all of this, it was time to read the rules. Easy to understand, as there aren’t too many rules at all in this cooperative game. basically it comes down to:

    Spend Action Points
    Roll for Smoke & Resolve Smoke / Fire / Explosions
    Roll for Points Of Interests (If Appropriate)

Each player may spend 4 AP’s. If he doesn’t spend all AP’s he get’s AP tokens, which he can save for a later turn. This way he can collect 4 AP’s, so he may have 8 AP’s to spend in one turn. Move 1 square will cost 1 AP. Open or close a door costs 1 AP. Carry a victim costs 2 AP’s per square. After the player has spend (or saved) his AP’s he gets to roll the two dice and place a smoke token to the corresponding square on the board. Then he has to resolve the smoke. Easy rule to keep this in mind is: smoke + smoke = fire. Fire + smoke = fire. Fire + fire = explosion. Basically this works the same as an outbreak in Pandemic. After the resolving the fire, a player has to role the dice again to place an POI token on the board (if a victim is missing or rescued).

Playing this game feels like Pandemic light. It’s easier to explain, and the theme will be more attractive to kids. Although the box says it’s 10+, I think a 6-year old should be able to play this game when he plays with an adult. And almost every six year old boy wants to play a firefighter, rescuing people. How this goes on for a six year old girl? I don’t know, but I guess she would like to be save by a tough firefighter. Also the saving of the action points for a later turn in the game is a nice twist. Fun family game, that plays fast and is easy to explain. And the fact that it is lighter then Pandemic, isn’t that strange at all. That’s because of all the fire!

=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 8
I love Flash Point. A good situation can turn bad easily, and that keeps the interest. There's no predicting where the fire will go, which makes sense as smoke moves through the building. You really have to decide where you spend your actions and hope for the best.

It's probably my favourite cooperative game, because it takes everyone to really look at the board and make the best decisions. Unlike Pandemic, or the Forbidden franchise (which I also love), where you can easily play on your own because everything is right there: you know where the problem is likely to appear next because the cards are right there. There's less randomness, and it feels less tense than Flash Point.

When we have one damage cube left in Flash Point, the tension is palpable. I don't remember being terribly stressed by Pandemic.
=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-=-
RATING: 7.5
A member of the alpha player cooperative game group.  One guy could definitely end up driving the bus here.  The base game is fun; the family game is irrelevant for the more serious gamers among you.

Like Pandemic, still inferior to Yggdrasil.
